<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">SCU2022</span> - Site specificity: Sculptural and installation interventions<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-SCU2022">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-fine-art.html">Department of Fine Art</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Terri Bird">Dr Terri Bird</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Terri Bird">Dr Terri Bird</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-SCU2022">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OHS1000.html">OHS1000</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/SCU1021.html">SCU1021</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/SCU1022.html">SCU1022</a></span> or SCU1611 or SCU1612, or permission from the Unit Coordinator</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit will introduce a broad range of sculptural and installation approaches that artists employ when responding to different spatial contexts. Students will explore different genres of public art from a sculptural perspective and will respond to a choice of sites on campus. Students will explore and articulate different processes to achieve their ideas and present their proposal for individual and group feedback.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Understand and discuss different functions of public art works, sculptural interventions and the audiences relationship to space;</li>
<li>Develop presentation skills to communicate and articulate and developed proposal and critique the work of others;</li>
<li>Apply skills and understanding of the process for making a public art proposal or intervention;</li>
<li>Produce photographic and model works that apply knowledge and skills related to the materiality and scale of public sculpture;</li>
<li>Critically analyse the possibilities of responses to the site, scale and material choices;</li>
<li>Analyse key elements to a site and the relationship of its function to the community;</li>
<li>Reflect on the role of contemporary sculptural and spatial practices;</li>
<li>Understand and apply the rules of occupational health and safety appropriate to the discipline practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Assessment is 100% by folio at mid-semester and end of semester. The folio will be comprised of works produced during the duration of the unit, and may also include students works made independently of the unit and a journal which will document on-going progress and research in relation to the unit project.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 4 hours of taught studio and 8 hours of independent study and studio practice.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS2620</span> - The age of the Samurai<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS2620">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-history.html">History</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Adam Clulow">Associate Professor Adam Clulow</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Adam Clulow">Associate Professor Adam Clulow</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2620&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS2620">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of first-year Arts units.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit explores the history of Japan and East Asia via an examination of the figure of the samurai. The focus is broadly on the period from 1185 to 1867 when Japan was ruled by a succession of warrior regimes but the unit will also explore the evolution of samurai images and representations primarily in film but also in books, anime, manga, and video games. The central concern is with the evolution of the figure of the samurai across this long period and with the constant tensions between the ideals put forward about the way of the warrior and the actual realities of samurai life.  We will explore the samurai from varied perspectives by considering questions of status, identity, politics, gender, and economics.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>identify key political transformations across Japanese history as well as Japan's place in the wider region;</li>
<li>explain processes of identity formation and the power of national myths;</li>
<li>analyse the social hierarchies that underpinned the emergence of the samurai class;</li>
<li>cultivate independent research skills via the creation of a unit portfolio;</li>
<li>develop effective communication, team work, argumentation and critical reflection skills.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/global-asia">Global asia</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/history">History</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/japanese-studies">Japanese studies</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">NUT5004</span> - Food for dietetic practice<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 2, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-NUT5004">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-nutrition-dietetics-and-food.html">Department of Nutrition, Dietetics and Food</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Evelyn Volders">Evelyn Volders</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jorja Collins">Dr Jorja Collins</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUT5004&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-NUT5004">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUT5001.html">NUT5001</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUT5003.html">NUT5003</a></span>. Must be enrolled in course M6002.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>Please note: The teaching dates for this unit vary from the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census">standard teaching dates</a><span class="hbk-print-url">standard teaching dates (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census">http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census</a>)</span> for this teaching period.</p>
<p>Unit discontinuation and penalty dates for these units are different to other units taught in the same teaching period.</p>
<p>Please refer to the information available on the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/medicine/study/student-services/non-standard-dates">Faculty non standard teaching dates page</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Faculty non standard teaching dates page (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/medicine/study/student-services/non-standard-dates">https://www.monash.edu/medicine/study/student-services/non-standard-dates</a>)</span> to avoid <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/enrolments/change/add-or-discontinue-units">academic and financial penalties</a><span class="hbk-print-url">academic and financial penalties (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/enrolments/change/add-or-discontinue-units">https://www.monash.edu/enrolments/change/add-or-discontinue-units</a>)</span>.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is focussed on extending students' food composition, food therapeutic and food systems knowledge to support dietetic practice with integration and application in the practical and placement setting. There is extension of students' research and problem solving skills in managing placement based food service challenges. Students' personal and professional competencies are further developed. This unit supports fulfilment of prescribed competencies as outlined by the Dietitians Association of Australia. The teaching and learning strategies will encompass lectures, group teaching, tutorials, practical sessions, self-directed learning and a placement based project. Placement may take place outside of regular semester times. Students must have valid police check, WWC check and immunisation certificates in order to participate in clinical placements</p>
<p>The key themes explored in this unit are Theme 4: Food from Science to Systems and Theme 3: Fundamentals of Health and Disease, coupled with partial integration of content and application from Theme 1: Personal Development and Professional Practice and Theme 2: Determinants and Influences on Population Health and Nutrition.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Integrate food composition and practical food knowledge to a range of therapeutic applications to support dietetic practice.</li>
<li>Compare, contrast and evaluate food service systems across healthcare settings including key regulatory and accreditation systems relevant to food service management.</li>
<li>Demonstrate technical skills in analysis and evaluation of a food service system.</li>
<li>Formulate and communicate strategies to provide safe and nutritious food in food service settings.</li>
<li>Implement, evaluate and disseminate results of activities that support delivery of quality nutrition and food standards within a food service.</li>
<li>Apply research practice skills and innovative problem solving to food service management challenges.</li>
<li>Apply the principles of management in food service including organisational management, human resource management and production management.</li>
<li>Utilise reflection, professional and personal communication and teamwork skills.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Fieldwork</h2>
<div>
<p>Students will be allocated placement sites to conduct a food service project for 20 days. This placement will be arranged by the University however students will be responsible for travel and accommodation costs if required.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Written Placement Project report (4,000 words) &amp; Presentation (10 minutes) (40%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Food product marketing proposal (1,500 words) (15%)</li>
<li>Practical activities manual and reflection (1,500 words) (15%)</li>
<li>Oral presentation of training module for food service/health care staff (20 minutes) (10%)</li>
<li>Menu Analysis Executive Report (2,000 words) (20%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle: Professionalism Development Form (Hurdle)</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>There is an average of 12 hours per week allocated including contact and private study hours during the theory component. The placement is 20 days at 8 hours per day, thus averaged over a semester contributes an additional 12 hours per week. There is no exam for this unit. The placement in a food service setting may need to be outside of regular university semester times.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/dietetics">Dietetics</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BTM3290</span> - Independent study<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BTM3290">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-business-law-and-taxation.html">Department of Business Law and Taxation</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Abdul Majid Nabi Baksh">Dr Abdul Majid Nabi Baksh</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BTM3290&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BTM3290">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Students must have completed five units from the Department of Business Law and Taxation major, including <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BTW1042.html">BTW1042</a></span> and permission from the Chief Examiner following approval of research topic and suitable supervisor.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This elective is designed to allow students to conduct an independent study in the area of business law or tax under the supervision of a member of the BLT academic staff (the supervisor). The student will, with the guidance of the supervisor, identify a research project, prepare a proposal, collect data (which may involve library research or collection of empirical data or both) and write up a final report of about 6,000 words. The project may be a bibliography or annotated bibliography, journal entries or other kinds of short reflective pieces such as a book review or a research essay. The project may apply hypothetico-deductive interviews. No formal lectures will be held for this unit.</p>
<p>This unit will comprise a specially tailored course of reading and/or other activities that are agreed to by the student and the student's supervisor. The unit allows the supervisor and student the flexibility to design a course of study that enables the student to acquire specialised knowledge in his/her selected topic and the necessary research skills to access that knowledge.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>generate questions/aims/hypotheses within structured guidelines</li>
<li>collect and record self-determined information/data, choosing an appropriate methodology</li>
<li>evaluate information/data and the inquiry process using self-determined criteria developed within structural guide lines</li>
<li>organise information within the supervisors parameters</li>
<li>analyse information gaps stated by others.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester, typically comprising a mixture of one-on-one conferences with a supervisor and independent study. The unit requires on average contact between the supervisor and the student at least once every two weeks.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BTW3233</span> - Conventional and Islamic finance law<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BTW3233">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-business-law-and-taxation.html">Department of Business Law and Taxation</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Adnan Trakic">Dr Adnan Trakic</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BTW3233&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BTW3233">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BTW1042.html">BTW1042</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit covers the main areas of conventional and Islamic financial regulations. This includes aspects of the legal environment that affect financial decisions, transactions and relationships in both conventional and Islamic finance. Topics covered are chosen from the laws regulating the financing implications of different forms of business organisation; financial institutions and the financial institutions/customer relationship; cheques; the laws regulating business finance and security and guarantees.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>analyse conventional and Islamic finance law problems with the necessary awareness to plan and structure an appropriate answer</li>
<li>effectively apply problem solving strategies that includes clear presentment of a legal argument, and critical and creative thinking</li>
<li>identify, evaluate and implement appropriate strategies for resolution of conventional and Islamic finance law problems</li>
<li>be innovative in resolving conventional and Islamic finance law problems</li>
<li>be able to reference sources of information in written work.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 40% + Examination: 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">TDN2002</span> - Communication design theory<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-TDN2002">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-design.html">Department of Design</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Dion Tuckwell">Mr Dion Tuckwell</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Dion Tuckwell">Mr Dion Tuckwell</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=TDN2002&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-TDN2002">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/TDN1002.html">TDN1002</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit covers significant theories and readings specific to the discipline of communication design. The histories of print- and screen-based communication are studied, with particular consideration given to the social and technical changes that have influenced the development of communication design. Theories of communication, readability and authorship are considered. A particular focus lies with the technologies of typography and the evolution of the written word. Students will develop an appreciation of the history of the discipline and its social significance, in order to better understand contemporary communication design.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Understand the history and the prehistory of communication design;</li>
<li>Critically discuss different perspectives on the social significance of communication design;</li>
<li>Recognise historical and theoretical references in contemporary works of communication design;</li>
<li>Articulate an informed position in relation to key issues in communication design discourse; and</li>
<li>Analyse and discuss the social or disciplinary significance of works of communication design.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 3 contact hours plus 9 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">FNA2003</span> - 3D digital modelling for artists<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FNA2003">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-fine-art.html">Department of Fine Art</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Callum Morton">Professor Callum Morton</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Callum Morton">Professor Callum Morton</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FNA2003&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FNA2003">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/DWG1201.html">DWG1201</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OHS1000.html">OHS1000</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit introduces students to the use of 3D digital modelling software to explore the development, visualisation and production of objects. It will provide students with knowledge of how to build and manipulate digital models, using the following CAD (Computer Aided Design) software; Rhino (Rhinoceros 3D), MeshMixer &amp; 3D Coat. In addition to 'first principle' modelling, there will be an introduction to the creation of digital models using 3D scanning and photogrammetry technology. Students will also be exploring visualisation imaging using complimentary rendering software Vray, and will be producing physical outputs of their digital models utilising laser.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Develop diverse methods for observing, analysing and collaborating in the production of work;</li>
<li>Apply techniques to investigate expressive possibilities arising from intensive discourse and interactions with fellow art, design and architecture students</li>
<li>Confidently interpret, represent and respond to diverse modes of practice, contexts, shared languages, skills and experience related to diverse visual-based disciplines;</li>
<li>Engage collaboratively with other project contributors, effectively articulating ideas and concepts, resulting in creative resolution;</li>
<li>Conceptualise, design and create site-specific work(s);</li>
<li>Critically analyse the effect/impact of project ideas and proposals, including engagements with the community;</li>
<li>Understand and apply the rules of occupational health and safety appropriate to the discipline practice, and be able to collaborate and cooperate safely and productively with peers.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 4 contact hours plus 8 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">TAD4503</span> - Advanced art theory<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-TAD4503">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-fine-art.html">Department of Fine Art</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<!-- TBA -->TBA
        
        
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<!-- TBA -->TBA
        
        
      
    <br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-TAD4503">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Admission to Honours year</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit aims to help students develop their knowledge and understanding of various key theoretical writers and concepts relevant to advanced studies in contemporary art. Prevailing critical theories and terms are outlined in order to open up research venues considered particularly productive for the art researcher's own personal directions. The unit is designed as a training for independent research and encourages students to investigate a wide range of ideas circulating in contemporary visual culture.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Be aware of current discourses in a range of disciplines which bear on contemporary artistic production;</li>
<li>Be able to pursue critical arguments with a sense of their ideological relativity;</li>
<li>Assess the bias of an investigative method, considering gender, class and ethnicity;</li>
<li>Understand methodology as a critique of method and be able to practice criticism in their chosen field;</li>
<li>Identify assumptions inherent in the formulation of critical questions and cultivate caution against prejudicing the outcomes of research by foreclosing on the terms of inquiry;</li>
<li>Be ready to explain the basis of art works not merely as the outcome of practical constraints but the expression of cultural values.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Two written papers (30% and 70%)</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 3 hours of lectures and tutorials and 9 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">ACS3730</span> - Financial accounting C<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ACS3730">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-accounting.html">Department of Accounting</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Karen Odendaal">Ms Karen Odendaal</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ACS3730&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ACS3730&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ACS3730">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ACS2740.html">ACS2740</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit covers various aspects of financial accounting and builds on the principles introduced in prior financial accounting units. It provides a detailed examination and/or more detailed exploration (than AFS2730/<span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ACS2730.html">ACS2730</a></span> or AFS2740/<span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ACS2740.html">ACS2740</a></span>) of applying reporting standards (IFRS) in a financial reporting environment, with the focus on conceptual framework; preparation and presentation of financial statements; provisions, contingent liabilities and contingent assets; revenue recognition; income taxes (including deferred tax); leases, non-current assets held for sale and discontinued operations; the effects of changes in foreign exchange rates and hedging; employee benefits; share-based payments; financial instruments; and earnings per share.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning objectives associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>critically analyse the conceptual framework with regards to the objective of general purpose financial reporting; the specific information needs of users, as well as the general information needs of other users; the qualitative characteristics and underlying assumption of useful financial information; the appropriate definitions of elements and their recognition criteria</li>
<li>discuss the key aspects of the conceptual framework (as described in objective 1) as applied to the preparation and presentation of financial statements, as well as the various spectrum of accounting topics dealt with in this unit</li>
<li>discuss, apply, calculate and explain the detailed requirements relating to various IFRS topics, including recognition, measurement, disclosure and presentation of these topics: provisions, contingent liabilities and contingent assets; revenue recognition; income taxes (including deferred tax); leases, non-current assets held for sale and discontinued operations; the effects of changes in foreign exchange rates and hedging; employee benefits; share-based payments; financial instruments; and earnings per share</li>
<li>identify, discuss and apply the detailed requirements of the various IFRS topics included in this unit to integrated accounting case studies and practical scenarios, in order to identify and solve all the related issues regarding a variety of IFRS problems included in one scenario</li>
<li>apply critical thinking, problem solving and presentation skills to individual and/or group activities dealing with financial according and demonstrate in an individual summative assessment task the acquisition of a comprehensive understanding of the topics covered by ACS3730.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 40% + Examination: 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_it"><span class="unitcode">FIT5186</span> - Intelligent systems<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FIT5186">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_it">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-it.html">Information Technology</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chung-Hsing Yeh">Associate Professor Chung-Hsing Yeh</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FIT5186&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FIT5186">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-suzhou.html">Suzhou</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Fundamental mathematics</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>This unit is only available to students enrolled in the double award Master International/Master of Information Technology Systems with South East University, China</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit introduces main techniques widely used in intelligent software systems to students in the Master of Information Technology Systems course with the Network Computing major. Specifically, it focuses on the techniques in relation to network structures. Main topics covered include neural network models, supervised learning and classification, unsupervised learning and clustering, fuzzy logic, intelligent decision analysis, optimum network flow modelling, and recommender systems.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit, students will have a knowledge and understanding of:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Explain the principles and theoretical underpinning of intelligent systems</li>
<li>Develop intelligent models and conduct experiments for solving a specific problem</li>
<li>Describe and evaluate the advantages and limitations of intelligent models and techniques for solving a wide range of practical problems</li>
<li>Analyse and evaluate current research developments in intelligent systems</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 60%; In-semester assessment: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>Two hours of lectures</li>
<li>One 2-hour laboratory</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 8 hours independent study per week for completing lab and project work, private study and revision.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">MIC3022</span> - Molecular virology and viral pathogenesis<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MIC3022">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Gregory Moseley">Dr Gregory Moseley</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Gregory Moseley">Dr Gregory Moseley</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MIC3022&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MIC3022">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>At least two of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2052.html">BMS2052</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2062.html">BMS2062</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2011.html">MCB2011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2022.html">MCB2022</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MIC2011.html">MIC2011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MIC2022.html">MIC2022</a></span>, MOL2011 and MOL2022</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit will cover molecular aspects of virus replication and introduce students to the diversity of viruses and the mechanisms used by viruses to infect hosts and cause disease, with an emphasis on host-pathogen interactions. The focus will be on human and animal viruses and will include the most up-to-date research as well as areas of major worldwide concern, such as emerging viral infections. The molecular strategies used by different types of viruses for infection, replication and transmission will be presented. Theory will be underpinned by practical experiments that will provide experience in working with viruses, in addition to a variety of current virological techniques used in research and diagnostic laboratories.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the fundamental principles underlying infection by all major groups of viruses, and apply this knowledge to understand infection and disease caused by specific pathogenic viruses;</li>
<li>Explain how viruses interact with target host cell components and
defence mechanisms and how this can lead to disease;</li>
<li>Describe specific strategies used to limit and control viral infections;</li>
<li>Demonstrate practical skills and knowledge of molecular virology laboratory techniques;</li>
<li>Apply knowledge of molecular virology and viral pathogenesis to critically analyse interpret and discuss experimental data and scientific literature;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a range of scientific communication skills, through oral presentations, participation in workshops and written laboratory reports.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Mid-semester test (45 mins): 10%</p>
<p>Written theory examination (3 hours): 50% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Practical class assessment: 40% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>A total of 12 hours per week including 6 hours of directed learning (such as lectures, practicals and workshops) and 6 hours of private study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/microbiology">Microbiology</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MGF5923</span> - Public policy<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MGF5923">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>

         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>

<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MGF5923">

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit assists students to understand how the public policy process operates and the role of stakeholders in policy development. Public policy process theory is discussed in the light of specific cases, and related to a broad range of practitioner experience. Case studies in Australian public policy will be analysed within this course.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>define a range of models and theories that help explain how public policy is made</li>
<li>analyse the role of government institutions and processes in policy making</li>
<li>analyse how governments engage with stakeholders in public policy processes.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>

Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">PHH2022</span> - Culture, society and health<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PHH2022">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-south-africa-school-of-health-sciences.html">South Africa School of Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jackie Witthuhn">Dr Jackie Witthuhn</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<!-- TBA -->TBA
        
        
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PHH2022&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PHH2022">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of the following units: HSC1081, HSC1112, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH1081.html">PHH1081</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH1112.html">PHH1112</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>HSC2022, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PBH2003.html">PBH2003</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit will explore how individual and population experiences of health are shaped by culture and society. The unit draws on key sociological and anthropological theories and concepts to reveal explanations for health in respect of larger socio-cultural realities and political processes. Students will be encouraged to foster skills in critical deconstruction of Western representations of culture to arrive at an appreciation of various 'ways of knowing', including Indigenous scholarship. There will be a focus on global health and in particular, Indigenous people, place, culture and health.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Apply key principles of sociological and anthropological thought to the lived experience of individuals and populations.</li>
<li>Apply the themes associated with the sociological imagination to examine the social production, construction and organisation of health locally and globally.</li>
<li>Apply sociological theories as analytical tools to critically examine cultural, social, political and economic factors influencing health.</li>
<li>Critically examine and evaluate aspects of culture and society with which they are familiar (as well as historical representations) in order to extend their understanding of the socio-cultural structures, institutions and processes relevant to health globally.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Individual journal (1,200 words) (15%)</li>
<li>Individual analysis (1,500 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Group presentation (15 minutes) (15%)</li>
<li>Individual essay (2,000 words) (40%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle: 80% attendance at tutorials.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>3 hours contact time per week (1 hour lecture 2 hour tutorial / workshop) PLUS 9 hours of private study hours per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/public-health---south-africa">Public health - South Africa</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">MEC5885</span> - Energy efficiency and sustainability engineering<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MEC5885">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-mechanical-and-aerospace-engineering.html">Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Davies">Professor Chris Davies</a>

        (Malaysia)

</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MEC5885&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MEC5885">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>None</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>None</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>None</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit explores the theory and practice of the supply of energy, energy management and auditing, and the design of sustainable energy facilities. It deals with the systems needed to create low-energy, sustainable buildings, including passive solar design, energy-efficient heating and air-conditioning, and combined heat and power.</p>
<p>In addition, it includes coverage of transport energy and energy economics. Case studies from a variety of energy-focused industries such as building services, environmental engineering, heating, ventilation, and air conditioning (HVAC) and architectural technology will be discussed.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate the concepts and dimensions of energy sustainability to the development of future sustainable energy technologies.</li>
<li>Generate the strategy of sustainable management of energy by creating organisational structure and corporate culture as well as transforming goals and allocation of resources in the process of energy conservation and management.</li>
<li>Apply sustainable energy management practices, from improving energy efficiency to utilising renewable resources to minimise risk in buildings and power plants.</li>
<li>Appraise the sustainable energy development level by indicators of development in line with the implementation of energy efficiency audit, energy management risk, and environmental investments risk assessment.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 40%</p>
<p>Final Examination (2 hours): 60%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>3 hours lectures, 2 hours labs/tutorials and 7 hours of private study per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/mechanical-engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_it"><span class="unitcode">FIT3036</span> - Computer science project<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FIT3036">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_it">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-it.html">Information Technology</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Marc Cheong">Dr Marc Cheong</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FIT3036&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FIT3036&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FIT3036">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT2004.html">FIT2004</a></span> or FIT3140</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>CSE3301, FIT3144</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is intended to provide practical experience in designing, developing and testing a non-trivial computer science project. Projects are generally software-based, although sometimes they may involve hardware development or investigation of theory. Projects cover the whole process of software (or hardware) development, from analysis through design to implementation and testing. Comprehensive written documentation on the project is required. Students are assigned in groups to a project supervisor. There are no lectures in this unit, although students will be expected to attend regular meetings with their project supervisor.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>evaluate and select research methods and techniques of data collection and analysis appropriate to a particular project and practice these ethically and professionally;</li>
<li>search, access and analyse research literature as part of the process of developing solutions to problems;</li>
<li>communicate in written and oral form the proposed deliverables of a project and reflect upon their value and the likelihood of success;</li>
<li>develop, demonstrate and explain a software prototype or model;</li>
<li>develop and test a substantial piece of software or hardware;</li>
<li>explain and reflect upon the purpose, operation, success and value of the developed project in writing and orally;</li>
<li>write a report explaining methodology, outlining their contributions and the contributions of others, and documenting the developed project from appropriate perspectives, for instance that of a user, researcher or developer.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Projects are assessed by individual project supervisors.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>One 1-hour project meeting</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 11 hours independent study per week for completing project work and private study.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">BCH3021</span> - Cellular organisation: Organelle structure and function in health and disease<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BCH3021">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mark Prescott">Associate Professor Mark Prescott</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Phil Bird">Professor Phil Bird</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BCH3021&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BCH3021">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BCH2011.html">BCH2011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BCH2022.html">BCH2022</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2021.html">BMS2021</a></span>, MOL2011 or MOL2022 or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2011.html">MCB2011</a></span> OR <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2022.html">MCB2022</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BTH3741.html">BTH3741</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides an advanced understanding of the structure-function of the individual structural organelles and components of the cell in the context of cell biology and disease processes. Topics include the cytoskeleton, the formation of the membranes, the intracellular trafficking of proteins, the cellular internalization/export of proteins. Overriding themes of this subject are:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>to view the cell as a dynamic unit composed of a series of interacting organelles</li>
<li>to understand the cell as a semi-independent biological entity in constant contact and communication with the extracellular environment and with other cells in multicellular organisms.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the structure of eukaryotic cells and explain the function of key organelles;</li>
<li>Outline how different organelles are formed and positioned within cells and how these organelles respond to a changing environment;</li>
<li>Explain the mechanisms that target and move proteins to the correct organelle and how protein mis-localisation and organelle dysfunction may lead to human disease;</li>
<li>Discuss how the application of fluorescence-based imaging and other technologies increases our understanding of cells, organelles and cellular proteins;</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to organise, plan and successfully execute laboratory experiments relevant to molecular cell biology, as well as analyse and report the results in a meaningful way;</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to conduct literature-based research, identify key knowledge and concepts and build coherent arguments and explanations either in writing or in oral presentations;</li>
<li>Work effectively as a pair or in a group to achieve academic tasks collaboratively with respect for each other.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 50%  (Hurdle)</p>
<p>In-semester quizzes on lecture material: 10%</p>
<p>Small group/practical work: 30% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Evaluation of mentored literature review (Essay): 10% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Two 1-hour lectures and one 4-hour practical/tutorial/self-directed learning exercise per week</li>
</ul><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3974</span> - European integration and security<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3974">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-politics-and-international-relations.html">Politics and International Relations</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ben Wellings">Dr Ben Wellings</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ben Wellings">Dr Ben Wellings</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3974">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of second-year Arts units. It is highly recommended that students only take this unit after they have completed two cornerstone units in Politics or International relations.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>War and security have been crucial motors of international relations, not least in Europe the birthplace of the Westphalian state system. The European Union is commonly seen to have been an antidote to war, ushering in an era of Kantian peace; a view powerfully endorsed by the awarding of the Nobel Prize to the EU in 2012. Despite the strength of this view, recent research suggests it is possible to look at the relationship between peace and European unity differently. In fact, European unity has been propelled by war since 1945: not just at the founding moment at the end of the Second World War (NATO, EEC, WEU), but by anti-colonial nationalists pushing European powers towards pro-active European policies, and in EU responses to the conflicts in the former Yugoslavia (OSCE, CFSP), Iraq, Libya and the challenges posed by refugee movements and global terrorism. An unintended consequence of the logic of deeper integration has been the consolidation of a European identity amongst some elites, whilst political and popular support for the EU has weakened. This last development poses serious questions about the future shape the state system in what remains a major player in regimes of global governance and security.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>identify and appraise the concepts, parameters and architecture of European security in a global context;</li>
<li>distinguish between the concepts of traditional and non-traditional security and recognise the competing paradigms in the security studies literature;</li>
<li>explain and analyse the course and dynamics of European integration since the end of the second World War;</li>
<li>integrate one set of academic literature (European integration theory and history) with another (European security);</li>
<li>undertake a research analysis of an important aspect of European integration or a major security policy area, utilising primary and secondary-source materials with written feedback.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/international-relations">International relations</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">AMG5409</span> - Communication research<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-AMG5409">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>

         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>

</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-AMG5409">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>APG4409, APG5409, AMG4409</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit equips students with applied skills in research design, research methods and ethical research practice. Students are taught the elements of good research design, various qualitative and quantitative research methods, and the marks of ethical research practices.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of the unit, students will be able to demonstrate:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Knowledge, skills and attributes necessary for understanding and engaging in advanced research;</li>
<li>Increased understanding of the methods of communication research;</li>
<li>Increased understanding of approaches to planning and designing research, and to writing and editing research;</li>
<li>Increased knowledge, skills, and attributes necessary for independent research, enhanced capacity to formulate and research communication issues, to analyse and evaluate arguments, and to understand critical approaches to the planning, writing and editing of research;</li>
<li>Enhanced intellectual independence, and greater self-reliance and critical distance in academic and professional research activity;</li>
<li>Significantly increased capacity to design, manage, and carry out research projects.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/communications-and-media-studies">Communications and media studies</a></p>
</div>

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit allows students to build on the critical and analytical skills developed through the major by having the opportunity to develop a research project tailored to their disciplinary interests. Special permission to undertake this unit must be obtained from the co-ordinator of the major.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>After successfully completing this unit students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Develop a research proposal</li>
<li>Develop a research strategy</li>
<li>Identify the key resources relevant to the topic</li>
<li>Demonstrate understanding of the research topic, critical engagement with relevant theoretical material, analysis of sources and or data through the completion of an extended research essay.</li>
</ol>
</div>
