<h1 class="banner_law"><span class="unitcode">LAW3112</span> - Corporations law<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-LAW3112">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_law">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-law.html">Law</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
    
      
        
        Semester 1 :
        <a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Normann Witzleb">Associate Professor Normann Witzleb</a>
<br/>
    
      
        
        Semester 2 :
        <a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Weiping He">Dr Weiping He</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=LAW3112&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=LAW3112&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-LAW3112">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB (Hons) course in 2015 or later:</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1111.html">LAW1111</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1114.html">LAW1114</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1112.html">LAW1112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1113.html">LAW1113</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2101.html">LAW2101</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2112.html">LAW2112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2111.html">LAW2111</a></span></p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB course prior to 2015:</p>
<p>LAW1100 OR LAW1101 and LAW1102 or LAW1104; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit critically examines the body of legal rules that govern the formation, management, financing and winding up of Australian corporations. Specific topics include: choice of the corporate business form, formation and characteristics of a corporation, the corporate constitution, corporate finance, share structure and membership, constitution and powers of the corporate organisation (board and general meeting), corporate authority, governance of the corporation, directors' duties, shareholders' remedies, administration and winding up of the corporation.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>critically evaluate the law relating to corporations in a broader regulatory, social or economic context;</li>
<li>demonstrate the intellectual and practical skills needed to interpret legal conclusions and professional decisions ;</li>
<li>identify, research, synthesise and evaluate relevant legal, factual and policy issues, including interpreting and applying relevant provisions of the Corporations Act;</li>
<li>demonstrate cognitive and creative skills in approaching legal issues and generating appropriate responses and developing new understandings;</li>
<li>engage in critical analysis and make reasoned and appropriate choices among alternatives; and</li>
<li>communicate effectively and persuasively to specified audiences.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Tutorial attendance and participation requirement (Hurdle requirement, with no marks allocated to it. Failure to satisfy the requirement will result in a zero mark for task 2).</li>
<li>Written assignment, 2000 words: 40%</li>
<li>Final exam (2 hours plus 30 minutes reading and noting time): 60%</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS2380</span> - Australia: Migrant nation<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS2380">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-history.html">History</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Christina Twomey">Professor Christina Twomey</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mia Treacey">Dr Mia Treacey</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2380&amp;tpCode=WS-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Winter semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS2380">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Winter semester 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of first-year Arts units.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>The unit may be offered as part of the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html">Winter Arts Program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Winter Arts Program (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html">http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html</a>)</span>.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit examines migrations of people across the globe as a potent force in the making of the modern world, with a focus on Australia since the mid-eighteenth century to the present day. The movement of people is considered in the context of major transformations in criminal codes, government legislation, labor force requirements, resources booms, and the disruptions of revolution, war and armed conflict. Groups to be studied include convicts, assisted immigrants, indentured labourers, gold-seekers, displaced persons, refugees and asylum seekers. The efforts of governments to shape their populations, through mechanisms such as transportation, the regulation and restriction of migration, deportation, internment and border control will also be studied.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>identify and explain the major forces that have shaped the movement of people across the globe to Australia since the mid-eighteenth century;</li>
<li>distinguish between transportees, indentured labourers, slaves, assisted migrants, displaced persons, refugees and asylum seekers;</li>
<li>analyse the migration patterns and developments that have influenced the shifting demography of Australia through problem based learning research projects;</li>
<li>develop oral and written communication skills in constructing evidence-based arguments using a variety of primary and secondary sources</li>
<li>reflect critically on what they have learnt.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/history">History</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/international-studies">International studies</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FIT3003">

<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of FIT1004 or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT2094.html">FIT2094</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Automation and the use of technological tools have resulted in the accumulation of vast volumes of data by modern business organisations. Data warehouses have been set up as repositories to store this data and improved techniques now result in the speedy collection and integration of such data. OLAP technology has resulted in the faster generation of reports and more flexible analysis based on the data repositories. This unit will explore the concepts of data warehousing and OLAP, covering the data processing technological requirements for data warehousing and OLAP and will provide hands on experience on designing data warehousing and OLAP systems.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>design multi-dimensional databases and data warehouses;</li>
<li>use fact and dimensional modelling;</li>
<li>implement online analytical processing (OLAP) queries;</li>
<li>explain query optimisation and its impact on multi-dimensional design;</li>
<li>create business intelligence reports using data warehouses and OLAP.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 60%; In-semester assessment: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>Two hours of lectures</li>
<li>One 2-hour laboratory</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 2 hours of personal study per one hour of contact time in order to satisfy the reading and assignment expectations.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/business-analytics">Business analytics</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/business-information-systems">Business information systems</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/computational-science">Computational science</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/data-science">Data science</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides students with the opportunity to encounter a challenging research environment through the interaction of philosophical paradigms and extension of theoretical knowledge and acquisitions of skills to facilitate the undertaking of a research project. The unit will build upon knowledge gained in core undergraduate research units. Students will be allocated a research supervisor to begin formulating research questions and methodology for subsequent study.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>evaluate and utilise appropriate philosophical foundations of research;</li>
<li>distinguish and critique quantitative and qualitative methodologies;</li>
<li>develop and utilise research skills in the following areas:
<ul>
<li>advanced online searching;</li>
<li>documentation management;</li>
<li>data collection methods and analysis; and</li>
</ul></li>
<li>begin formulating research question and proposed study.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Written assessment (3,500 - 4,000 words) (60%)</li>
<li>Oral presentation (40%)</li>
</ul>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">MEC3454</span> - Thermodynamics and heat transfer<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MEC3454">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-mechanical-and-aerospace-engineering.html">Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Davies">Professor Chris Davies</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mahdokht Shaibani">Dr Mahdokht Shaibani</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/engineering/juliosoria">Professor Julio Soria</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Professor Julio Soria (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/engineering/juliosoria">https://www.monash.edu/engineering/juliosoria</a>)</span> (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Hung Yew Mun">Associate Professor Hung Yew Mun</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MEC3454">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MEC2405.html">MEC2405</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit aims to develop a fundamental understanding of the processes by which heat and energy are inter-related and converted and by which heat is transferred. The unit will review major principles of energy conversion and the modes of heat transfer. The basic laws of thermodynamics and the governing equations for heat transfer and thermodynamics will be introduced and subsequently used to solve practical engineering problems involving thermodynamics and heat transfer. The unit will also cover fundamental design principles of power generation systems and heat exchangers.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Apply fundamental equations to establish mathematical relationships amongst commonly encountered thermodynamic properties.</li>
<li>Use psychrometric charts to analyse and quantify air conditioning processes.</li>
<li>Analyse the performance of combustion processes utilised to generate energy and recognise the importance of greenhouse effects.</li>
<li>Evaluate the performance of internal combustion engines.</li>
<li>Identify modes of heat transfer in energy-related processes.</li>
<li>Appraise engineering problems involving heat conduction, convection and radiation by selecting and applying appropriate tools to model the problem.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 40%</p>
<p>Final Examination (2 hours): 60%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>3 hour lectures and 3 hours practice sessions/laboratories (this may alternate with 2 hours lectures and 4 hours practice sessions/laboratories) and 6 hours of private study per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/mechanical-engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">ASP1010</span> - Earth to cosmos - introductory astronomy<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ASP1010">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-physics-and-astronomy.html">School of Physics and Astronomy</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jasmina Lazendic-Galloway">Dr Jasmina Lazendic-Galloway</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jasmina Lazendic-Galloway">Dr Jasmina Lazendic-Galloway</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ASP1010&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ASP1010">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>No formal background in astronomy or astrophysics is required.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>ASP1010 can only be completed prior to <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ASP2011.html">ASP2011</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ASP2062.html">ASP2062</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit focuses on concepts that will allow students to gain understanding of key astrophysical phenomena. The topics covered include the night sky, the historical development of astronomical knowledge, our solar system, comets and asteroids, the sun, exoplanets, other stars, stellar remnants such as black holes, the Milky Way, other galaxies, quasars, dark matter, and cosmology in general.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the evolution and general properties of planets, solar systems, stars, and galaxies.</li>
<li>Explain celestial and planetary motions across the night sky using naked eye observations and planetarium software.</li>
<li>Reflect on the scale of the universe and earth's place in it.</li>
<li>Execute experiments involving telescopes and other simple apparatus and analyse, interpret and evaluate the results arising from them.</li>
<li>Demonstrate ability to analyse and solve problems using quantitative and qualitative analysis.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 40%</p>
<p>Workshops: 30%(Hurdle)</p>
<p>Assignments: 30%</p>
<p>Hurdle requirement: Students must achieve a pass mark in the workshops to achieve an overall pass grade.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>The workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours spread across the semester (roughly 12 hours per week) - approximately an even mixture of attendance at scheduled activities and self-scheduled study time. Learning activities comprise a mixture of instructor directed, peer directed and self-directed learning, which includes face-to-face and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/astrophysics">Astrophysics</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/physics">Physics</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BFW3652</span> - Corporate treasury and credit management<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BFW3652">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-banking-and-finance.html">Department of Banking and Finance</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Teh Chee Ghee">Dr Teh Chee Ghee</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Teh Chee Ghee">Dr Teh Chee Ghee</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BFW3652&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BFW3652">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BFW1001.html">BFW1001</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit explores the roles, responsibilities and organisation of the treasury and credit control functions in non-financial firms, best practices and approaches to managing such functions, the performance measurement thereof, and the finance principles applying to corporate treasury and credit management.</p>
<p>Areas covered include the theory and practice of financial risk management, cash and liquidity management for non-financial institutions, capital markets and funding, formulation of credit extension policy, credit evaluation, monitoring and control, debt collections, behavioural finance aspects of combating late payment of receivables, debts recovery, and using internet technology and tapping into the capital markets, credit rating agencies and other market intelligence, to make informed cash and credit management decisions in today's borderless, fast-paced and challenging business environment.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>define and describe the scope of corporate treasury and credit management and how effective cash and credit management can support and add-value to the corporation</li>
<li>understand the roles and responsibilities of the corporate treasurer and the credit controller and identify approaches to managing a corporate treasury and credit control department within the organisation and within the department itself</li>
<li>apply financial knowledge and skills to identify and implement appropriate strategies to manage key corporate treasury and credit risks</li>
<li>develop financial and behavioural skills in the implementation and application of efficient cash and cash flow management, credit control strategies to optimise the cash flow of the businesses</li>
<li>apply critical thinking, problem solving and presentation skills to individual and/or group activities dealing with corporate treasury and credit management and demonstrate in an individual summative assessment task the acquisition of a comprehensive understanding of the topics covered in BFW3652.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 40% + Examination: 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">IDE4118</span> - Industrial design studio 8 (major project 2)<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">18 points, SCA Band 2, 0.375 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-IDE4118">

         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-design.html">Department of Design</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>

<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=IDE4118&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-IDE4118">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IDE4117.html">IDE4117</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>IDE4108</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is the second of the major project sequence. Students are expected to continue with research initiated in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IDE4117.html">IDE4117</a></span>, and develop a time frame which details prototype construction in consultation with a supervisor and course coordinator. Project must have appropriate aspects to serve as a vehicle to demonstrate the student's professional understanding and capabilities as well as appropriate complexity to enable the student to professionally undertake and present it within time and resource limitations of the unit.  Documentation must be completed to a professional standard. Regular group and individual critiques are undertaken as the project and the thinking underlying it develop.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Be able to develop and refine their industrial design project from the conceptual stage undertaken in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IDE4117.html">IDE4117</a></span> Major Project (Industrial Design) Part One through to a prototype presentation, demonstrating a high level of capability;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a comprehensive understanding of the discipline and its professional practices, with particular reference to the social, cultural and aesthetic aspects of their investigation;</li>
<li>Have a high level of knowledge of the contemporary discourse in design and industrial design and to be able to position their work relative to it;</li>
<li>Be able to debate and/or defend their practice in an informed critical appraisal;</li>
<li>Cultivate high ambitions to perfect their practice of industrial design;</li>
<li>Observe and employ occupational health and safety principles and rules appropriate to studio practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>36 hours per week including 8 contact hours plus 28 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">APG5690</span> - Applied translation<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">

<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>In this unit students  apply theoretical approaches to practical translation tasks in a variety of textual genres. The unit aims to develop students' abilities to translate texts of increasing levels of complexity and specialisation. The unit explores translation across a range of media.  It complements <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/APG5048.html">APG5048</a></span> Translation for Special Purposes, adopting a similar approach to learning and assessment, but exploring different genres and professional contexts.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>identify and discuss problems that specialised textual genres pose for translation;</li>
<li>critically apply theoretical approaches to formulate strategies in response to translation problems;</li>
<li>use a variety of specialised tools to translate effectively;</li>
<li>employ effective strategies to translate multimodal texts, such as audiovisual and web-based texts.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 70% + Exam: 30%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/interpreting-and-translation">Interpreting and translation</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/translation">Translation</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">EAE4060</span> - Advanced field geology<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-EAE4060">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate, Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-earth-atmosphere-and-environment.html">School of Earth, Atmosphere and Environment</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Laurent Ailleres">Dr Laurent Ailleres</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Laurent Ailleres">Dr Laurent Ailleres</a>
<br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Robin Armit">Dr Robin Armit</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=EAE4060&amp;tpCode=T2-58&amp;tpYear=2019">Trimester 2</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-EAE4060">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Trimester 2 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Enrolment in the Master of Science</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/EAE5060.html">EAE5060</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>The unit is offered in a non-standard teaching period.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit aims to teach the skills of geological mapping in two classic field locations of Australian geology, in Broken Hill (poly-deformed and high-grade metamorphic terrane) and Bermagui (poly-deformed, highly complex terrane).  In both field camp, the emphasis will be on observing, recording, and interpreting geologic phenomena in a natural environment.  Students will draw on a theoretical background of lectures and laboratory studies in first, second and third-year geology to analyse real rocks in the real world. Students will use their observations and interpretations to construct geological maps and cross-sections and determine the geological history of complex poly-deformed terrane.  The concept of key locality for observation and critical thinking for correlation between key locality will be introduced and applied to produce map and cross sections of highly complexly deformed terranes.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit,  students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>produce structural geological maps;</li>
<li>observe and interpret the distribution of lithologies and structures in the field;</li>
<li>correlate observations and interpretations at the outcrop scale to produce consistent map and cross-sections;</li>
<li>determine the relationship between structure and metamorphic assemblages;</li>
<li>visualise complex three dimensional geometries;</li>
<li>unravel the geological history of complexly deformed terranes;</li>
<li>determine overprinting relationships from field geology;</li>
<li>communicate results in a written report;</li>
<li>work in a team environment and communicate of results with peers;</li>
<li>equip students with discipline-specific knowledge and expertise appropriate for post-graduate research in the field; equip students with discipline-specific knowledge and expertise enabling them to take their place as professional geologists in industry or government organisations; develop their field mapping techniques.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Fieldwork exercises Broken Hill: 45%</p>
<p>Fieldwork exercises Bermagui: 35%</p>
<p>Presentation: 10%</p>
<p>Report: 10%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Total of 80 hours for Broken Hill</li>
<li>Total of 40 hours for Bermagui</li>
<li>24 hours independent study</li>
</ul><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p>Master of Science in Earth Science</p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB (Hons) course in 2015 or later:</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1111.html">LAW1111</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1114.html">LAW1114</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1112.html">LAW1112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1113.html">LAW1113</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2101.html">LAW2101</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2112.html">LAW2112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2111.html">LAW2111</a></span></p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB course prior to 2015:</p>
<p>LAW1100 or LAW1101 and LAW1102 or LAW1104</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB (Hons) course in 2015 or later:</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW3111.html">LAW3111</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW4332.html">LAW4332</a></span></p>
<p>LAW2100 or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2101.html">LAW2101</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span>; LAW2200 or LAW2201 and LAW2202</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The focus of the unit is the major steps in litigation. Using the Rules of the Supreme Court of Victoria, the chronology of a civil proceeding from the decision to sue until the matter is ready for trial is examined.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Students who successfully complete the unit should:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Identify the key principles, concepts and policies relating to the resolution of civil disputes.</li>
<li>Show an ability to exercise professional judgment in recognising and responding appropriately to ethical issues that arise in the context of civil dispute resolution.</li>
<li>Critically evaluate the available processes of civil dispute resolution and the steps and documentation of civil litigation.</li>
<li>Demonstrate effective written communication skills by clear and persuasive articulation and application of procedural rules and principles and by drafting basic court documents (such as pleadings, affidavits or submissions).</li>
<li>Demonstrate effective oral communication through class discussion and collaborative effectively on assessable tasks (for example in the activity focused on alternative dispute resolution).</li>
<li>Utilise feedback to reflect on and assess their capabilities and performance.</li>
<li>Demonstrate an ability to work with a high degree of autonomy and  professionalism.</li>
<li>Demonstrate cumulative knowledge and skills to propose appropriate solutions to complex legal problems.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours plus 30 minutes reading and noting time): 50%</p>
<p>Legal Writing Exercise: 20%</p>
<p>Quiz: 10%</p>
<p>Alternative dispute resolution activity and reflection: 20%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week (more when taught intensively). Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">CIV6886</span> - Infrastructure geomechanics<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">0 points, SCA Band 2, 0.000 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CIV6886">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-civil-engineering.html">Department of Civil Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jeff Walker">Professor Jeff Walker</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Qianbing Zhang">Dr Qianbing Zhang</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=CIV6886&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CIV6886">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CIV5886.html">CIV5886</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>In this unit the learner will gain skills and knowledge on the interaction between the geomaterials and structural components that make up most infrastructure systems. From buildings and bridges, to tunnels, roads/railroads, dams, and embankments, the learner will determine the interaction among various elements, and design appropriate solutions accordingly.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Determine the properties of geomaterials and structural components relevant for the assessment of interaction.</li>
<li>Assess the structural and geomechanical components available to address the expected interaction.</li>
<li>Determine the interaction between structural and geomaterials using computational and analytical methods.</li>
<li>Design appropriate solutions for infrastructure systems by incorporating governing interactions.</li>
<li>Describe the limitations of developed solutions and prepare a formal report.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 60%</p>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 40%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>3 hours lecture/practice and 9 hours of private study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p>Civil Engineering</p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">CHM1051</span> - Chemistry 1 advanced<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CHM1051">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>

</li>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CHM1051">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>October intake 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>VCE Units 3 and 4 Chemistry (Study Score &gt;=37), or an ATAR &gt;=90</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CHM1011.html">CHM1011</a></span>, CHM1031</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>CHM1051 has been designed for students who have demonstrated a strong aptitude for chemistry during secondary studies, eg. a VCE Chemistry Study Score &gt;=37. On completion of this unit, students will have gained an understanding of atomic structure, how atoms and molecules interact with each other and how this affects their bonding, reactivity, 3D structure and physical properties. A number of important topics such as stoichiometry, intermolecular forces, thermodynamics, kinetics, equilibria, and electrochemistry will be developed in order to prepare students for a deeper exploration of chemistry. The concepts developed within the lectures and workshops are complemented through an extended laboratory program where students will have the opportunity to develop analytical techniques and design their own experiments to solve a range of chemical problems.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Employ quantum mechanics to describe features of atomic structure and the construction of the periodic table of elements;</li>
<li>Interpret the relationships between electronic structure and bonding exploring a wide range of molecular structures;</li>
<li>Investigate aspects of stereochemistry such as isomerism and chirality;</li>
<li>Distinguish differences between ideal gases and real gases;</li>
<li>Recognise factors which give rise to polarity and studying how this affects intermolecular bonding;</li>
<li>Define the first and second laws of thermodynamics and apply enthalpy and entropy;</li>
<li>Discuss factors which give rise to chemical kinetics;</li>
<li>Apply acid-base chemistry in the understanding of dynamic equilibria;</li>
<li>Discuss the basic principles of redox reactions and electrochemistry;</li>
<li>Foster the acquisition of practical skills by exploiting an inquiry-based approach to the chemistry laboratory experience;</li>
<li>Formulate hypotheses and design chemical experiments to synthesise and collect unique data using a range of sophisticated apparatus and technologies;</li>
<li>Apply recognised methods for interpreting chemical data;</li>
<li>Communicate chemistry, and discuss the social and environmental responsibility of chemists in the global community.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 55% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Laboratory work: 35% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Online assessment: 10%</p>
<p>Hurdle requirements: To pass this unit a student must achieve a minimum score of 50% in the laboratory practical component and a minimum of 30% for the end-of-semester exam.</p>
<p>Supplementary assessment is not available for the lab practical component.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Two 1-hour workshops, one hour of directed independent study and one 4-hour laboratory class per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/applied-microbiology">Applied microbiology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/biotechnology">Biotechnology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/chemistry">Chemistry</a></p>
<p>Materials science</p>
<p><a href="../aos/medicinal-chemistry">Medicinal chemistry</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/physiology">Physiology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/tropical-environmental-biology">Tropical environmental biology</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MGF5960</span> - Organisations: people, purpose and structure<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MGF5960">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-management.html">Department of Management</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mary Anderson">Dr Mary Anderson</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mary Anderson">Dr Mary Anderson</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MGF5960&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MGF5960&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MGF5960">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (Evening)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (<a href="index-bymode-off-campus.html">Off-campus</a>)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (Evening)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in course B4001, B5001, B5002, B6006, B6009, B6012, B6019 or C6006, or be granted permission from the Chief Examiner to undertake this unit.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit will provide a foundation from which to explore the broad nature of organisations and the function of management in relation to its people, purpose and structure. Students will critically explore organisations from a multi-level organisational perspective to develop student understanding and appreciation of current debates and challenges in relation to managing organisations. The unit will commence with an overview of an organisation's human resources and its role in achieving its strategic objectives. The function of managers in achieving strategic goals will also be analysed including the manager's role in guiding the development of the internal environment and structure in order to creatively respond to the complexities of its external environment. Understanding how to ethically, and sustainably, construct, lead and mobilise a diverse workforce in a globally complex world is an important requirement of the modern manager.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>analyse the broad nature of organisations and the function of management in relation to its people, purpose and structure</li>
<li>critically analyse the importance of aligning individual, the team and the organisation's contribution in attaining organisational goals</li>
<li>assess the role of ethics and social responsibility in determining the culture and internal practices of an organisation in the overall conduct of its business</li>
<li>critically apply and evaluate contemporary management theory and research and generate creative business solutions to current organisational issues</li>
<li>understand the impact of complex external environments on organisational function.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 50% + Examination: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">MEC4444</span> - Industrial noise and control<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MEC4444">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-mechanical-and-aerospace-engineering.html">Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Davies">Professor Chris Davies</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Wing Kong Chiu">Professor Wing Kong Chiu</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Tan Ming Kwang">Dr Tan Ming Kwang</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MEC4444&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MEC4444">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MEC3453.html">MEC3453</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/TRC3200.html">TRC3200</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Fundamentals of sound and sound propagation, wave equation, Helmholtz equation, absorption, impedance and intensity, silencers. Transmission from one medium to another, applications and optimisation. Transmission through walls, mass law, coincidence and resonance. Sound transmission in the atmosphere, inverse square law, excess attenuation. Radiation of sound, directivity. Sound in enclosed spaces. Noise sources, noise reduction techniques, noise legislation and regulation, acceptable noise levels, hearing conservation, measurement and analysis of noise, design for low noise.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit, should are expected to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Calculate basic noise measurement quantities (sound pressure levels, sound power levels and sound intensity level);</li>
<li>Model the propagation of sound in a duct and in free-space;</li>
<li>Analyse the fundamentals of reactive noise attenuation devices;</li>
<li>Explain the concept of transmission loss:</li>
<li>Explain the concepts of direct and reverberant noise field in a close-environment;</li>
<li>Combine the concepts of noise source, noise path and noise measurement to examine the impact of a given noise source on its environment.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 40%</p>
<p>Final Examination (2 hours): 60%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>2 hours of lectures, 2 hours of laboratory/tutorial classes and 8 hours of private study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/mechanical-engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_it"><span class="unitcode">FIT1048</span> - Fundamentals of C++<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FIT1048">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_it">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-it.html">Information Technology</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Cheryl Howard">Cheryl Howard</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FIT1048&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FIT1048">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>FIT2071</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit introduces programming fundamentals and the C++ language to students. The unit provides a foundational understanding of program design and implementation of algorithms to solve simple problems. Fundamental programming control structures, built in and complex data-types and mechanisms for modularity will be presented in C++. This unit also places a focus on object-oriented design principles, using object-oriented design as a process for program design and problem solving. More advanced object-oriented programming topics such as inheritance and polymorphism will also be covered. Other C++ fundamentals such as pointers and the STL will be presented, as will implementations of algorithms and data structures used in problem solving.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>design, implement, compile, execute and debug programs using fundamental C++ constructs;</li>
<li>apply fundamental programming control structures, including conditional statements, iteration and recursion to solve programming problems;</li>
<li>apply object-oriented design principles, including inheritance and polymorphism, to solve programming problems;</li>
<li>create C++ programs using pointers to demonstrate an understanding of efficient memory use and management;</li>
<li>troubleshoot C++ program code using an Integrated Development Environment and its tools.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 50%; In-semester assessment: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>Two hours lectures</li>
<li>Two hours laboratories</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 2-3 hours of personal study per one hour of lecture time in order to satisfy the reading, tute, prac and assignment expectations.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/games-development">Games development</a></p>
<p>Mobile apps developments</p>
<p><a href="../aos/web-development">Web development</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">NUR5217</span> - Advanced paediatric nursing<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-NUR5217">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-nursing-and-midwifery.html">School of Nursing and Midwifery</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Beverley Copnell">Dr Beverley Copnell</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Beverley Copnell">Dr Beverley Copnell</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-NUR5217">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The paediatric nurse requires a diverse knowledge and skill base to assess and manage patients in a variety of settings. The unit enables the student to develop proficiency in the holistic management of sick children, beyond the beginning specialist level, and prepares students for leadership roles in their practice area.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>describe the aetiology, clinical manifestations and pathophysiology of a range of diseases/conditions observed in children;</li>
<li>plan and implement appropriate, evidence based, therapeutic nursing interventions related to the management of paediatric patients;</li>
<li>plan and implement appropriate, evidence based, therapeutic nursing interventions related to the management of children with complex health needs;</li>
<li>critically analyse the clinical issues supporting and complicating advanced practice in paediatric nursing;</li>
<li>analyse the collaborative interdisciplinary team approach to management of paediatric patients.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Take home examination (30%)</li>
<li>Written assignment 1 (3,000 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Written assignment 2 (5,000 words) (40%) (hurdle)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/nursing">Nursing</a></p>
<p>Nursing and midwifery</p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">PHH1052</span> - Health care systems: Global and local<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PHH1052">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-south-africa-school-of-health-sciences.html">South Africa School of Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Nwamaka Nwogwugwu">Nwamaka Nwogwugwu</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Samson Muyanga">Dr Samson Muyanga</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PHH1052&amp;tpCode=OCT-MSA-01&amp;tpYear=2019">October intake</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PHH1052&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PHH1052">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>October intake 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in an Undergraduate Degree</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>HSC1052.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides an introduction to health care systems (local and global), including key features and principles as well as the role of policy, politics, ideologies, resources and funding in their design and operation. The unit also utilizes relevant current events to generate discussion and debate around policy approaches to specific issues and the politics of health and social care.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Recognise key features of health and social care systems.</li>
<li>Identify key principles and processes underpinning the design of health and social care systems.</li>
<li>Describe the roles of health professionals in the health system.</li>
<li>Explain the role of key factors influencing the design and operation of health and social care systems (including politics, ideologies, resources and funding).</li>
<li>Compare health systems with regard to structure, performance, and context.</li>
<li>Work effectively in a group to plan and complete tasks collaboratively.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Individual presentation (10 minutes) (15%)</li>
<li>Group presentation (15 minutes) (20%)</li>
<li>Written assignment (2,500 words) (40%)</li>
<li>Quizzes x 3 (in-class) (multiple choice) (25%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle: 80% attendance at tutorials.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>4 hours per week (2 hour lecture, 2 hour tutorial) PLUS 8 hours of private study hours per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/public-health---south-africa">Public health - South Africa</a></p>
</div>

         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>

<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MDC5001&amp;tpCode=FY-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Full year</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MDC5001&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MDC5001&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MDC5001">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Full year 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MDC4002.html">MDC4002</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit represents the third of a three-part design project and students are expected to continue with the research initiated in Design project (part two). Defined designs are expected to be detailed resulting in an assessable design outcome. Regular group and individual critiques of the project will be undertaken as the project and the thinking underlying it develop. Both the intentions of students and the results of their work are debated in group discussions and critical sessions. Students will be expected to demonstrate a strong capability to detail design issues.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Be able to demonstrate a capability to independently select and apply relevant design methodology to resolve and detail their design project;</li>
<li>Be able to debate and/or defend their outcomes in an informed critical appraisal;</li>
<li>Demonstrate an extensive understanding of their design discipline and its professional practices, within the scope of their investigation;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a capability to lead, manage and plan complex design projects within their selected field;</li>
<li>Understand and be able to apply the rules of occupational health and safety appropriate to the unit of study.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>36 independent study hours per week including weekly meetings with project supervisors and regular seminars.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
