<h1 class="banner_law"><span class="unitcode">LAW4242</span> - Introduction to transitional justice<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-LAW4242">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_law">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-law.html">Law</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ronli Sifris">Dr Ronli Sifris</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ronli Sifris">Dr Ronli Sifris</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-LAW4242">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB (Hons) course in 2015 or later:</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1111.html">LAW1111</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1114.html">LAW1114</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1112.html">LAW1112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1113.html">LAW1113</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2101.html">LAW2101</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2112.html">LAW2112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2111.html">LAW2111</a></span></p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB course prior to 2015:</p>
<p>Pre-requisites: LAW1101 Introduction to legal reasoning and LAW1104 Research and Writing</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>None</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>None</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The term 'transitional justice' refers to the various judicial and non-judicial measures that may be implemented in order to redress a legacy of human rights abuse. Such measures include criminal prosecutions, truth commissions, reparations and different forms of institutional reform. This unit will begin by providing an overview of transitional justice; it will consider the meaning of the term "transitional justice" and provide a framework through which the concept may be understood. The unit will then engage in a more detailed discussion of the actual transitional justice mechanisms before moving on to consider a number of case studies in order to ground students' understanding of the subject matter in concrete examples. In addition to exploring the transitional justice programs implemented in different countries, the unit will also engage in a comparative analysis of the various case studies and will examine a number of cross-cutting themes, such as gender and transitional justice.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>understand the meaning of "transitional justice" and its application in different contexts.</li>
<li>recognise the complexities and context specific nature of a comprehensive transitional justice program.</li>
<li>analyse a transitional justice program from an interdisciplinary perspective.</li>
<li>critically evaluate the use of different transitional justice mechanisms in a number of different contexts.</li>
<li>examine the applicability of transitional justice mechanisms within the Australian context.</li>
<li>communicate effectively and persuasively both verbally and in writing.</li>
<li>conduct comprehensive interdisciplinary research.</li>
<li>learn and work both autonomously and collaboratively and use feedback to improve their own capabilities and performance.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Class Presentation: 10%</p>
<p>AND</p>
<p>Optional Assignment: 30% (1,500 words) OR</p>
<p>Write-up of class presentation (ungraded hurdle requirement)</p>
<p>AND</p>
<p>Take-home exam: 90% / 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MBA5225</span> - Global executive MBA innovation I<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 3, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MBA5225">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Patrick Butler">Professor Patrick Butler</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Patrick Butler">Professor Patrick Butler</a>
<br/>
</p>

<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MBA5225&amp;tpCode=MBA-TP3-01&amp;tpYear=2019">MBA Teaching Period 3</a>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MBA5225">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>MBA Teaching Period 3 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MBA5221.html">MBA5221</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MBA5222.html">MBA5222</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MBA5223.html">MBA5223</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MBA5224.html">MBA5224</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MBA5226.html">MBA5226</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Global Executive MBA Innovation I unit comprises two component topics: China Business Strategy and Global Executive MBA Business Project II.</p>
<p>China Business Strategy is co-created with faculty at a leading Chinese business school and taught at their campus. The topics covered include China's transformation and its global implications, comparative analysis of Chinese and other business models, and strategies for entering the China market. Expert guest speakers and local company visits provide opportunities for engagement with industry.</p>
<p>Global Executive Business Project II is the second in the series of applied consulting projects, in which teams of students undertake an international business project for an Australia-based business in the international market. Assignments in this module emphasise innovation and technology, and can involve market feasibility assessment, resourcing projects, evaluation of global best practice or business relationship development. The international market research and related business consulting skills developed earlier will be applied.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals of this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>explore and evaluate the political, economic and commercial issues relating to the role and influence of China and the implications for Australia-based business</li>
<li>demonstrate the ability to analyse and synthesise a complex, international business situation and develop appropriate recommendations</li>
<li>demonstrate the ability to manage a consulting client relationship and provide a professional presentation and report that integrate academic learning and business outcomes.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average six/eight hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">APG5401</span> - Media empires and entrepreneurs<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-APG5401">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-communications-and-media-studies.html">Communications and Media Studies</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mugdha Rai">Dr Mugdha Rai</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mugdha Rai">Dr Mugdha Rai</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=APG5401&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-APG5401">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>ATS4720, APG4401</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit engages with the challenges facing the traditional media companies at a time when the mass-market and advertising business models that have long sustained them are under assault from new digital production and distribution technology that is fragmenting audiences and enabling smaller, more entrepreneurial organizations to compete against bureaucratic 'empires'. How do companies such as News Corporation, Channel Nine or Fairfax respond to the threats and opportunities posed by the new digital media businesses like Google, Apple iTunes and Facebook, and community activist projects such as Wikipedia that are leading and exploiting changes triggered by the digital revolution.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon completion of this unit students are expected to demonstrate an ability to;</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Critically analyse the business models of a variety of traditional media companies and the challenges and opportunities posed by new digital media;</li>
<li>Assess government policy responses to issues arising from new digital technology, media convergence and fragmentation of audiences;</li>
<li>Understand key debates surrounding transformation of public media, such as the Australian Broadcasting Corporation;</li>
<li>Engage in discussion informed by current media research and theory about the changing media environment in Australia and internationally;</li>
<li>Conduct independent research in the field of communications and media;</li>
<li>Think critically and conceptually about contemporary media industries and how they relate with content producers and audiences.
In addition, students taking APG5401 should be able to demonstrate additional conceptual ability in written work.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/communications-and-media-studies">Communications and media studies</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/cultural-and-creative-industries">Cultural and creative industries</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">OCC1011</span> - Professional issues<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-OCC1011">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-occupational-therapy.html">Department of Occupational Therapy</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ted Brown">Associate Professor Ted Brown</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Luke Robinson">Mr Luke Robinson</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=OCC1011&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-OCC1011">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-peninsula.html">Peninsula</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in course M3001.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><ul>
<li>You are required to provide evidence of completing a Standard First Aid course;</li>
<li>You are required to provide evidence of compliance with FMNHS immunization policy requirements to Student Services;</li>
<li>You are required to provide evidence of Working with Children approval to Student Services;</li>
<li>You are required to provide evidence of Fit to Work / Police Check to Student Services.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit will provide students with the skills necessary to describe the role of an occupational therapist as distinct from other health professionals. Students will learn to demonstrate appropriate professional behaviour and beginner's competency with specific early clinical skills. The unit will support students to develop an awareness of the legal, cultural and ethical issues of practice, and begin to understand and articulate some of the challenges faced by clients/consumers of health services.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<p>Theme 1: Personal and Professional Development</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>describe ethical and legal issues pertinent to a practicing occupational therapist;</li>
<li>demonstrate effective communication and interview skills for practice;

<p>Theme 2: Population Society and Health</p></li>
<li>consider concepts of disability and appreciate the impact of disability upon the individual;

<p>Theme 4: Applied Practice</p></li>
<li>develop competent pre-clinical skills in client handling, equipment use and prescription, and the correct use of mobility techniques;</li>
<li>examine safety and basic infection control issues in the workplace;</li>
<li>apply task and activity analysis to the occupational therapy practice context.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Assessment</p>
<ul>
<li>Lived Experience Reflective Essay (2,500 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Professional Issues Essay (2,500 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Class Tests x 2 (2 x 1 hour) (20% each x 2 = 40%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle requirements:</p>
<ul>
<li>Attendance at 80% of unit tutorials, practical skills sessions and seminars is required to pass this unit.</li>
<li>Completion of disability experience (e.g., visual impairment, limited mobility) (2 hours).</li>
<li>Professional conduct: Students are required to demonstrate professional behaviour in communication (written or verbal) with department staff and clinical educators in order to pass the unit.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Lecture component: 2 hours per week, Tutorial/Practicum component: 2 hours per week, Private study: 8 hours per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/occupational-therapy">Occupational therapy</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BFF3751</span> - Derivatives 1<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BFF3751">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-banking-and-finance.html">Department of Banking and Finance</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Philip Gray">Professor Philip Gray</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BFF3751&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BFF3751&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BFF3751">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BFF1001.html">BFF1001</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BFF2140.html">BFF2140</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit examines the institutional features of futures and options markets, the use of futures, options and other derivatives in arbitraging, trading and hedging, and pricing of these instruments.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>discuss the operations of derivatives markets</li>
<li>evaluate the options and futures markets for hedging and trading purposes</li>
<li>demonstrate how to price and value standards futures and options contracts and other derivatives</li>
<li>implement trading strategies and measure positions.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 50% + Examination: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">MEC4418</span> - Control systems<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MEC4418">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-mechanical-and-aerospace-engineering.html">Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Davies">Professor Chris Davies</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Hoam Chung">Dr Hoam Chung</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Tan Chee Pin">Assoc Professor Tan Chee Pin</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MEC4418">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MEC3457.html">MEC3457</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MAE3408.html">MAE3408</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/TRC3600.html">TRC3600</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Instruction on the basics of automatic control design, including analysis and design techniques (with MATLAB/SIMULINK). Assumes students have the ability to form and use classical and state-space models of linear systems, can calculate their responses in time and frequency domain, and have experience in using MATLAB. Control system design through root-locus, frequency response, direct pole-placement, and state estimation, with concepts of linear systems, controllability, and observability. Introductions to robust stability, PID control design, digital systems, and optimal control design methods will also be provided.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Apply fundamental concepts and skills with advanced control design techniques.</li>
<li>Appraise the response of single-input-single-output dynamic systems and describe various performance specifications in the time and frequency domains.</li>
<li>Apply classical control theories and design methods to simple linear systems in time and frequency domains.</li>
<li>Apply the fundamentals of linear systems theory and basic control design methods to dynamic models described in state-space representations.</li>
<li>Analyse control design problems using computer-aided design tools.</li>
<li>Synthesise system analysis, design, and performance evaluation to complete the implementation of a controller on digital hardware.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 40%</p>
<p>Final Examination (3 hours): 60%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>One 1-hour lecture, one 2-hour lecture, one 2-hour practice class and 7 hours private study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/mechanical-engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3899</span> - Jazz arranging: Contemporary arranging techniques for small groups to large ensembles<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3899">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-sir-zelman-cowen-school-of-music.html">Sir Zelman Cowen School of Music</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jordan Murray">Mr Jordan Murray</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jordan Murray">Mr Jordan Murray</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3899">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS2902.html">ATS2902</a></span></p>
<p>This unit is only available to students enrolled in a Bachelor of Music single or double degree.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit introduces students to jazz arranging styles and methodologies for small and large ensembles. Through listening tasks and score analysis, the unit explores various arranging concepts including form, instrumental range, register, blend, voicing techniques, rhythm-section writing as well as score preparation using notation software. Students then apply newly learned skills to the formulation and development of musical works, gaining practical feedback and experience via in-class performance workshops.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit, the students are able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate fundamental understanding of jazz arranging styles and methodologies as informed by historical and contemporary practices;</li>
<li>Critically evaluate, analyse and discuss jazz compositions and arrangements from written score and audio media;</li>
<li>Apply arranging concepts to the formulation and development of musical works.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/composition-and-music-technology">Composition and music technology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/ethnomusicology-and-musicology">Ethnomusicology and musicology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/music-performance">Music performance</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">FOR5006</span> - Traffic medicine<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FOR5006">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-forensic-medicine.html">Forensic Medicine</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sanjeev Gaya">Dr Sanjeev Gaya</a>
<br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Richard Bassed">Associate Professor Richard Bassed</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sanjeev Gaya">Dr Sanjeev Gaya</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Quota applies</p>
<p>This unit is quota restricted. Selection is on a first-in, first enrolled basis. For further information please contact the Postgraduate Course Administrator via email <a href="mailto:mnhs-forensicmedicine@monash.edu">mnhs-forensicmedicine@monash.edu</a> or phone 03 9684 4115.
      
      
      </p><p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=FOR5006&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FOR5006">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-southbank.html">Southbank</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (Online)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>This is a postgraduate course restricted to registered medical practitioners.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The aim of this unit is to present the medical issues applicable to road safety. The topics covered include the law and policing practices, driving skills and the impact of alcohol, other drugs and medical conditions on these skills, the effects of ageing on fitness to drive, interpretation of traffic injuries,   the principles of traffic engineering and road trauma epidemiology.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the history of road trauma and analyse the efficacy of counter measures introduced to combat the road toll;</li>
<li>Evaluate the relationship between road safety legislation and policing practices to traffic medicine and road safety;</li>
<li>Predict and evaluate the effects of a range of medical conditions upon driving skills with particular reference to licensing;</li>
<li>Outline  the known effects of various blood levels of alcohol and other drugs upon driving skills, and how their likely effects  apply to traffic medicine;</li>
<li>Identify road safety implications for ageing road users;</li>
<li>Interpret common injury patterns resulting from road trauma.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Hurdle introductory activity (0%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Essay assignments 4 x 15 % each (4,000 words total) (60%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Casebook/Workbook (2,000 words) (15%)</li>
<li>Case presentation (15 minutes) (25%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle Requirement: introductory activity; Unit Coord asks students to provide short bio outlining previous &amp; current experience/work etc</p>
<p>A pass in all elements of assessment is required. Students must obtain at least 50 % of the available marks for each element of assessment to pass the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>It is expected that students will need to undertake approximately 12 hours of study per week over the semester. This will include contact time, private study, assessment tasks (case studies, assignments) and, where possible, involvement in casework. Students are required to attend all workshops offered at the Department of Forensic Medicine during the semester.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Off-campus attendance requirements</h2>
<div>
<p></p><p>Compulsory 2 day workshop.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/forensic-medicine">Forensic medicine</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Additional information on this unit is available from the faculty at:</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="mailto:postgrad.courses@vifm.org">postgrad.courses@vifm.org</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS2335</span> - War and memory: Resistance, massacre and representation in second world war Italy<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS2335">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-languages-literatures-cultures-and-linguistics.html">School of Languages, Literatures, Cultures and Linguistics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Kevin Foster">Associate Professor Kevin Foster</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Kevin Foster">Associate Professor Kevin Foster</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2335&amp;tpCode=T3-58&amp;tpYear=2019">Trimester 3</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS2335">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-prato.html">Prato</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Trimester 3 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of first-year Arts units.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3135.html">ATS3135</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><ul>
<li>This unit is an <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad">international study program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">international study program (<a href="http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad">http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad</a>)</span> at Prato that requires an application to be enrolled and may incur additional cost.</li>
<li>The unit may be offered in <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census">non-standard teaching periods</a><span class="hbk-print-url">non-standard teaching periods (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census">http://www.monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census</a>)</span>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Through seminars, workshops and fieldwork this unit will examine how conflict has been represented, remembered and memorialised. The unit will have a specific focus on World War 2, the Italian Resistance, and the massacre of civilians in Tuscany and Emilia Romagna. The unit will consider how written and visual responses to these events, material forms of remembrance - monuments, memorials, museums,  and cemeteries in, or within reach of Prato - each function to memorialise the dead and how in articulating political and national ideologies, such sites acknowledge and incorporate countervailing ideologies and the contradictory testimony of survivors. The unit will unpack, examine and critique the complex inter-relations between media, memory and war, exploring how in pursuit of specific political and cultural goals, memories of conflict are created, constructed and recovered through an array of artistic and memorial forms. Students will be invited to move beyond a purely theoretical understanding of these issues by visiting museums, massacre sites and their memorials, examining and critiquing their mediation and creating a critical/creative response to one such site.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>demonstrate an understanding of the history of the second world war in Italy and a detailed knowledge of the massacres on Monte Sole and their subsequent remembrance;</li>
<li>articulate an advanced understanding of the roles of literature, film, arts and other media in shaping dominant modes of remembering conflict;</li>
<li>demonstrate an informed understanding of the nature and functions of propaganda, how it has been employed to advance political and ideological imperatives and how it combines with specific media to frame the remembering of differing conflicts;</li>
<li>demonstrate a sophisticated grasp of how material forms of remembrance, monuments, memorials, cemeteries, places of commemoration, are informed by ideology and function as media;</li>
<li>apply an advanced understanding of theories of memory, histories of conflict and developments in the media to explore the complex inter-relations of media, memory and war in relation to the second world war in Italy and the massacres at Monte Sole.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement. + Additional requirements + This unit will be taught intensively at Prato</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu.au/pubs/2018handbooks/courses/A2001.html">Bachelor of Global Studies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Bachelor of Global Studies (<a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/pubs/2018handbooks/courses/A2001.html">http://www.monash.edu.au/pubs/2018handbooks/courses/A2001.html</a>)</span></p>
<p><a href="../aos/cultural-competence">Cultural competence</a></p>

</div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">AZA3301</span> - Social inclusion internship: Working on migrant and refugee settlement in multicultural communities<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>

<div id="content_container_">

         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>

<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>

<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-AZA3301">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of second-year Arts units.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>AZA2301, MON2003, MON3001</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><ul>
<li>The unit has an internship component - contact the Unit Coordinator for further information.</li>
<li>The unit may be offered as part of the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html">Winter Arts Program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Winter Arts Program (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html">http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/winter-program.html</a>)</span>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>In the Social Inclusion Internship, students apply their academic and research skills to projects in the migration, refugees and multiculturalism sector.  Drawing on prior study of migration issues, the internship enables students to participate in the activities and projects of an approved host organisation.  It is an opportunity for students to gain first-hand experience of the culture and challenges of the workplace and to engage with the practical dimensions of migrant and refugee settlement and multicultural communities. The unit enables students to obtain practical workplace experience while gaining academic credit towards their degree.</p>
<p>Places are strictly limited and selection will be based primarily on academic merit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion all students will have:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Gained first-hand experience of the practical dimensions of migrant and refugee settlement and integration</li>
<li>Attained practical workplace interpersonal skills</li>
<li>Completed relevant research and/or job study that demonstrates their understanding of the complexities of migration</li>
<li>Developed knowledge of both the theoretical and practical challenges of immigration</li>
<li>Consolidated their skills in project formulation, implementation, analysis and reporting</li>
<li>Enhanced skills in managing and organising workloads for the completion of their internship research project and related assessment tasks</li>
<li>Enhanced their skills in critical reflection by engaging with the host organisation's positioning in terms of broader refugee, migration and multiculturalism issues</li>
<li>Strengthened their understanding of the interests of the various stakeholders in the migration sector</li>
<li>Enhanced their skills in critical thinking by undertaking an analysis of the implications of their own work and their host organisation's activities</li>
<li>Improved their ability for self-evaluation and reflective learning in the context of the workplace</li>
<li>Developed an understanding of the ethical issues one may encounter in the workplace and in the course of undertaking research</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/international-studies---south-africa">International studies - South Africa</a></p>
</div>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Enrolment in an approved Honours in the discipline of Regenerative medicine</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MIS4100.html">MIS4100</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit aims to develop analytical abilities and communication skills, as well as provide students with advanced knowledge in specific areas of Regenerative Medicine and Biomedical Science. Students will undertake an oral presentation of a current issue in the Biomedical/Biotechnological/Regenerative Medical field  and a written critique of a scientific article. Students will also undertake a component of work within their selected discipline that is unrelated to their specific research component and which involves some level of advanced theoretical training. Candidates may commence at the beginning of either first or second semester.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Critically review scientific literature in the discipline area of research;</li>
<li>Apply knowledge of current methodologies and concepts to appraise scientific literature in the discipline area;</li>
<li>Apply analytical and data analysis techniques relevant to the discipline area of research;</li>
<li>Effectively communicate concepts in the discipline area of research both in writing and orally.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Oral presentation of current issue in Biomedicine: 30%</p>
<p>Review of literature on an area of research unrelated to project (2000 words): 40%</p>
<p>Critique of scientific article: 30%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>To be advised by Honours co-ordinator</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p>Regenerative medicine</p>
</div>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Enrolment in this unit is subject to an application process. More information on this unit is available <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/graduate-industry-experience">here</a><span class="hbk-print-url">here (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/graduate-industry-experience">https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/graduate-industry-experience</a>)</span>. Applications must be submitted via this <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/application-and-approval-process">link</a><span class="hbk-print-url">link (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/application-and-approval-process">https://www.monash.edu/business/student-experience/career-development/industry-experience/work-integrated-learning/application-and-approval-process</a>)</span>.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is designed to provide students with the opportunity to put theory into practice in a business environment.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>compare and contrast theory and practice</li>
<li>apply theory to practice in a supervised environment</li>
<li>evaluate personal learning and personal development in a complex business environment</li>
<li>analyse complex business problems and to prepare and present innovative solutions.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>

</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Off-campus attendance requirements</h2>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">NUR5022</span> - Contemporary nursing in context 2<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-NUR5022">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-nursing-and-midwifery.html">School of Nursing and Midwifery</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Dawn Whithall">Ms Dawn Whithall</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Dawn Whithall">Ms Dawn Whithall</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUR5022&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUR5022&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-NUR5022">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5011.html">NUR5011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5111.html">NUR5111</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in one of the following course codes: 3966, M6016</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit has a strong focus on the theory and practice underpinning working with organizations, individuals, families, groups and communities.</p>
<p>Through discussion lectures, tutorials and interactive online sessions, students will be able to examine the skills in communication for the purpose of enhancing therapeutic relationships across the lifespan and ultimately ensuring quality health care are developed through studies in this unit.</p>
<p>The concepts of caring and helping in nursing within a therapeutic relationship, are explored. Students engage in in-depth analysis of the various human growth and development theories.</p>
<p>These theoretical concepts provide a foundation for students to explore aspects of the social model of health, with a particular emphasis on the provision of health care to vulnerable populations and nursing in a culturally diverse community.</p>
<p>Within this context the concepts of cultural competence and cultural safety are explored. The development of therapeutic engagement with vulnerable groups using these concepts will be central to the learning milieu of this unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Analyse the meaning of health and the broad principles of public health</li>
<li>Discriminate between the concepts of helping and caring in nursing practice.</li>
<li>Recognise the elements of therapeutic communication with particular reference to working with people from diverse cultural backgrounds and age groups</li>
<li>Critically analyse the impact of cultural diversity on health and illness behaviour</li>
<li>Incorporate the issues of cultural safety and cultural competence within nursing practice.</li>
<li>Determine barriers associated with access to, and equity in health care particularly as they relate to Indigenous Australians and people in different vulnerable groups</li>
<li>Identify population health outcome indicators particularly as they relate to Indigenous Australian and people in different vulnerable groups</li>
<li>Engage in self-reflection as a beginning step towards person-centred nursing.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Indigenous health assignment (5000 words) (50%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Written assignment (1500-2000 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Active learning engagement (20%)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Blended learning activities, including online and classroom sessions 6 hours/week:</p>
<p>Workshops: 4 X 3 hours and 2 X 1 hour,</p>
<p>Guided self-directed learning: 4 hours/week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/nursing">Nursing</a></p>
<p>Nursing and midwifery</p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS2296</span> - Musical theatre 1: History and form<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS2296">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-centre-for-theatre-and-performance.html">Centre for Theatre and Performance</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Fleur Kilpatrick">Ms Fleur Kilpatrick</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Fleur Kilpatrick">Ms Fleur Kilpatrick</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2296&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS2296">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of first-year Arts units.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>ATS2477, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3296.html">ATS3296</a></span>, ATS3477</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit combines a study of the history and formal structures of 'the Musical' with practical tuition and training in writing for Musical Theatre. It examines key theoretical frameworks for the study of Musical Theatre, and defines the formal characteristics of 'the Musical' in its Broadway and other manifestations. It embodies this knowledge in practical song writing and libretto writing workshops, including sessions with leading industry professionals, exploring the implications of particular choices in structure and score. Ultimately, the unit produces a full student-written work of musical theatre which is developed and performed in second semester in the unit, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS2297.html">ATS2297</a></span>/<span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3297.html">ATS3297</a></span> Musical Theatre 2 - Skills and Performance.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit students will have:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>an understanding of the conventions and traditions of twentieth-century musical theatre;</li>
<li>familiarity with the distinctive methodological issues involved in the study of the form, and of the languages appropriate to their articulation and analysis;</li>
<li>thorough knowledge of key works and developments in the field;</li>
<li>applied knowledge of formal structures and writings skills in musical theatre;</li>
<li>the ability to work collaboratively in a team throughout a creative process from inception to execution;</li>
<li>the capacity to articulate critical analyses in systematic written argument, and in clear and confident oral presentations.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/musical-theatre">Musical theatre</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">CIV2207</span> - Computing and water systems modelling<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CIV2207">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-civil-engineering.html">Department of Civil Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jeff Walker">Professor Jeff Walker</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ha Hong Bui">Dr Ha Hong Bui</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sina Alaghmand">Dr Sina Alaghmand</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CIV2207">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit covers basic spreadsheet computing skills and includes particular training in: mathematical tools such as matrix operations (eg solving simultaneous equations), curve fitting and trend lines, and numerical search techniques; user defined functions; user interface elements such as dialog boxes (using elements such as labels, text boxes, drop-down list boxes, spinners, etc) and VBA programming to automate spreadsheet functions. It also covers the following topics in water engineering: estimation of design rainfall; runoff processes; streamflow data and analysis; flood frequency analysis; reservoir operation and a major assignment on hydrology using spreadsheets.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe fundamental mathematical formulations for solving problems in civil engineering.</li>
<li>Apply spreadsheet computing and VBA programming tools to assist their designs in structure engineering, geomechanics and hydrology following the Australian and New Zealand standard.</li>
<li>Formulate typed brief reports detailing how they address and solve problems  that meets Australian and New Zealand standards.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Three projects: 45%</p>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 55%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component (assignments, tests, mid-semester exams, laboratory reports) and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit.  Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>3 hours lectures, 2 hours computer laboratories/practice classes and 7 hours of private study per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/civil-engineering">Civil Engineering</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MGS3210</span> - Organisational wellness<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MGS3210">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-management.html">Department of Management</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jennifer Nzonzo">Ms Jennifer Nzonzo</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MGS3210&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MGS3210">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MGS1010.html">MGS1010</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is designed to develop students' awareness of current theoretical perspectives on and of empirical evaluations of organisational initiatives designed to foster wellbeing at both the individual and organisational level. The unit will provide a macro-level framework for examining an organisation's social, ethical and environmental responsibility, followed by an examination of organisational level approaches to wellness including work/life initiatives and OH&amp;S initiatives. At the micro-level, the unit will address strategies individual employees may use to manage their own state of wellness.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>appreciate the relationship between the changing face of organisations into today's business environment and the need for managers to attend to organisational wellness</li>
<li>identify predictors and consequences of 'wellness' and 'toxicity' in the organisational context</li>
<li>describe and evaluate current organisational wellness initiatives</li>
<li>analyse and evaluate current theoretical frameworks of 'wellness' in order to understand and devise 'healthy' organisation initiatives.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">CDS1511</span> - Photographic art direction<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CDS1511">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-design.html">Department of Design</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Warren Taylor">Mr Warren Taylor</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Tobias Titz">Mr Tobias Titz</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=CDS1511&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CDS1511">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS1001.html">CDS1001</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/COL1001.html">COL1001</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OHS1000.html">OHS1000</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Photographic Art Direction will develop students' skills in their ability to manipulate and control photographic imagery via a sound understanding of digital camera technology, its associated software and studio lighting. It will build upon the foundation knowledge of photography gained as part of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS1001.html">CDS1001</a></span>.</p>
<p>This unit will expose students to the processes involved in the documentation of their own work, product photography, and other situations that require a sound knowledge of the photographic experience and how best to creatively negotiate its outcome. Students will become adept at being able to intuitively and creatively direct the narrative of a photograph through a competent use of language, composition, timing, light, props and camera technology.</p>
<p>Students will explore the potential of the camera in both studio and outdoor settings, and begin to understand the scope of creative possibilities and challenges each circumstance offers. They will be exposed to the work of leading exponents of the practice, both contemporary and historic. This unit will be of particular interest to students wishing to document folio content as well as those wanting to pursue a design career in advertising and marketing.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Understand key aspects of digital camera technology and its associated software;</li>
<li>Recognise the value of lighting, props, timing and exposure in the direction of a photographic outcome;</li>
<li>Create a number of photographic outcomes that use both studio lighting and natural lighting in their creation;</li>
<li>Direct and edit the narrative of a photograph through use of language, composition, timing, light, props and camera technology;</li>
<li>Discuss the value photographic art direction plays in the realm of communication design production;</li>
<li>Understand and apply the rules of occupational health and safety appropriate to the discipline practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 3 contact hours plus 9 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">IDN1002</span> - Industrial design studio 2<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 2, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-IDN1002">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-design.html">Department of Design</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Robbie Napper">Dr Robbie Napper</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mark Richardson">Dr Mark Richardson</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=IDN1002&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-IDN1002">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/COL1001.html">COL1001</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IDN1001.html">IDN1001</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>IDE1112, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IDE1802.html">IDE1802</a><span class="unitoffered">Not offered in 2019</span></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The aim of this unit is to understand and develop the students understanding and practical skill regarding the relationship between production and manufacture. The studio takes the student through a number of key studio based explorations that underpin and develop an understanding of the inter-relationship between a desired physical outcome and the manner of its production. This includes an appreciation of the core principles of manufacture methods and the impact upon the design of an object due to materiality. Students are encouraged to apply theoretical learning with an experimental approach to problem solving. Project work is presented in folio format, documented for production. Final design proposals are also undertaken in detailed model or prototypical form where appropriate.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>De-construct existing objects and products with intent of re-purposing them by understanding their making;</li>
<li>Design objects to meet certain physical criteria through the manipulation and exploitation of industrial multiple production processes;</li>
<li>Appreciate the practical and theoretical nature of industrial design, in particular the intimate relationship between rational processes and inspirational factors in design;</li>
<li>Identify, analyse, and interpret the general characteristics of design tasks;</li>
<li>Observe and employ occupational health and safety appropriate to studio practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>24 hours per week including 8 contact hours plus 16 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>
