<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MKM5251</span> - Innovation and entrepreneurship<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MKM5251">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-marketing.html">Department of Marketing</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MKM5251&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MKM5251">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Entrepreneurship and innovation are at the heart of modern business and social enterprises, nation states and society, driving economic development. Entrepreneurs in all situations identify opportunities that others cannot, and locate and configure resources in new ways to create value for stakeholders. This unit aims to provide students with an understanding of the processes, risks, rewards, motivations, and societal impacts of innovation in community, national, regional and global settings. It aims to inspire students to develop an entrepreneurial mindset, and to support their ability to innovate and build organisations for sustainable growth, benefiting all stakeholders. The course will explore the nature of enterprise, the role of the entrepreneur, and the role of innovation and technology in the entrepreneurial process. The focus is on capability development and growth, making it relevant for small and large, profit and not-for-profit ventures. It is aimed at nurturing individuals wishing to create innovative futures for themselves and their communities, and for markets and economies.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>explain how an entrepreneurial mindset and the associated skills supports innovation in the contexts of corporate venturing, social entrepreneurship and business start-up projects</li>
<li>apply an entrepreneurial mindset and skills to develop innovative solutions to complex community and business problems in conditions of uncertainty</li>
<li>recommend strategies to evaluate entrepreneurial skills, values and behaviours; and to further develop the entrepreneurial mindset of both themselves and others</li>
<li>demonstrate entrepreneurial and innovation related skills, including identifying and evaluating opportunities, solving problems creatively, communicating effectively, and influencing stakeholder groups</li>
<li>demonstrate the ability to work productively in teams to collaboratively explore opportunities, generate ideas and find and communicate solutions to a predefined challenge.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">IMM3031</span> - Molecular and cellular immunology<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-IMM3031">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Kim Murphy">Dr Kim Murphy</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mark Wright">Associate Professor Mark Wright</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=IMM3031&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-IMM3031">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM2011.html">IMM2011</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2052.html">BMS2052</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM3051.html">IMM3051</a></span> is highly recommended</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit examines in depth important features of development and function of the immune system in health and disease. Areas covered include development of the innate and adaptive immune system, antigen processing and presentation, maturation of the immune response, self tolerance and regulation. Advanced techniques in immunology will be presented including the relevance of genetic engineering. Skills will also be developed in searching and critically reviewing the literature, in assignment writing and oral presentation.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate the relevance of immunity to infection and disease;</li>
<li>Describe how differing arms of the immune response are integrated and regulated;</li>
<li>Define and compare how the innate and adaptive immune systems discriminate self from non-self and the mechanisms of self-tolerance;</li>
<li>Describe examples of how cutting edge technologies are used to study immunity;</li>
<li>Critically appraise data and the immunological literature and demonstrate skills in oral and written communication.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Two multiple choice examinations during semester (7.5% each): 15%</p>
<p>Tutorial assessments: 15%</p>
<p>Assignment: 10%</p>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 60% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Three 1-hour lectures and one 2-hour tutorial/self directed learning sessions per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/immunology">Immunology</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">OCC4082</span> - Advanced professional practice<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 2, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-OCC4082">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-occupational-therapy.html">Department of Occupational Therapy</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Lisa Knightbridge">Ms Lisa Knightbridge</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Karen Dixon">Karen Dixon</a>
<br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mong-Lin Yu">Dr Mong-Lin Yu</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=OCC4082&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-OCC4082">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-peninsula.html">Peninsula</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OCC4071.html">OCC4071</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OCC4071.html">OCC4071</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OCC4091.html">OCC4091</a></span>. Must be enrolled in the Bachelor of Occupational Therapy.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit comprises 9 weeks of fieldwork placement followed by on campus debriefing tutorials. The unit provides students with the opportunity to develop, integrate and enhance their practice skills to reach an entry level of competence in occupational therapy prior to graduation. By the end of the fieldwork placement students will be managing a caseload of clients independently. A learning contract developed in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OCC4081.html">OCC4081</a></span> will be used to guide fieldwork learning. A portfolio assessment will be used to encourage reflection, a self-directed approach to learning and to provide a record of professional competencies as these are developing.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate autonomous and competent application of all stages of the occupational therapy process to the level expected of a new graduate in occupational therapy as outlined in the Australian Minimum Competency Standards for New Graduate Occupational Therapists (ACSOT);</li>
<li>Apply professional attitudes and behaviours, and effective time and workload management strategies to occupational therapy practice;</li>
<li>Document personal and professional learning using a portfolio in preparation for professional accreditation;</li>
<li>Devise strategies to overcome service delivery constraints to provide effective occupational therapy intervention for clients in a fieldwork agency;</li>
<li>Collaborate, co-operate and communicate with other health professionals and health service providers to deliver effective and efficient practice;</li>
<li>Select and critique occupational therapy interventions on the basis of best available evidence;</li>
<li>Design and implement strategies for critical self-reflection, evaluation and improvement of own professional development;</li>
<li>Develop strategies to provide effective occupational therapy service considering the broad political, legal and industrial issues in the workplace, profession and client group;</li>
<li>Plan, implement and evaluate an occupational therapy service;</li>
<li>Critique an organization's key performance indicators and service delivery for continuous improvement and meeting the regulatory standards.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Fieldwork</h2>
<div>
<p>Clinical placement: 9 weeks (45 days).</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Reflective statement (2,000 words) (25%)</li>
<li>Written portfolio (8,000 words) (45%)</li>
<li>Oral portfolio exam (20 minutes) (30%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle requirement:</p>
<ul>
<li>80% attendance at tutorials, seminars and practical skills classes.</li>
<li>Satisfactory completion of fieldwork placement as assessed through the Student + Placement Evaluation Form - Revised (SPEF-R) (ungraded).</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/occupational-therapy">Occupational therapy</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">BIO3011</span> - Research methods in biology<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BIO3011">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-biological-sciences.html">School of Biological Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Matthew Hall">Dr Matthew Hall</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Matthew Hall">Dr Matthew Hall</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BIO3011&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BIO3011">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>12 points from level two BIO, BTH, ENV or GEN units and either <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/SCI1020.html">SCI1020</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/STA1010.html">STA1010</a></span> or STA2010 or permission.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Biological data is inherently variable. It is essential therefore that modern biologists be able to assemble and analyse these data to make important scientific advances. This unit will provide students with the framework to understand biological information, to test hypotheses, and to design robust experiments in biology. The ability to critique the methods used by scientific studies, make inferences from quantitative data, and optimize experimental approaches will benefit students taking a wide range of research and project-based units. Focus will be placed on interpreting and evaluating studies from the scientific literature and communicating biological findings to a range of audiences. This unit is a prerequisite unit for Honours in Biology and Genetics (<span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BIO4100.html">BIO4100</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BIO4200.html">BIO4200</a></span>).</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Construct, test, and evaluate scientific hypotheses in biology;</li>
<li>Design and optimize experiments for answering biological questions;</li>
<li>Choose and justify an appropriate analysis for a biological dataset and research question;</li>
<li>Critically evaluate biological findings and make inferences from analyses presented in the literature;</li>
<li>Effectively communicate the outcomes of biological programs and experiments to a range of audiences.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Theory examination (2 hours): 50%</p>
<p>Continuous assessment: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Two 1-hour lectures</li>
<li>The equivalent of 3 hours laboratory/tutorials per week</li>
</ul><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/ecology-and-conservation-biology">Ecology and conservation biology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/genetics">Genetics</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/plant-sciences">Plant sciences</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/zoology">Zoology</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">BCH3031</span> - Functional genomics and molecular medicine<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BCH3031">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Timothy Cole">Associate Professor Timothy Cole</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Peter Boag">Dr Peter Boag</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BCH3031&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BCH3031">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of the following <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BCH2011.html">BCH2011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BCH2022.html">BCH2022</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2062.html">BMS2062</a></span>, MOL2011, MOL2022, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2011.html">MCB2011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MCB2022.html">MCB2022</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BTH3752.html">BTH3752</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides an understanding of DNA as the genetic component of organisms and cells, encompassing the information content, the organisation of DNA sequences, and the expression of this information into RNA and proteins. Topics include global aspects of genome organisation and expression outcomes (genomics and proteomics, respectively). Other themes include the molecular diagnosis and treatment of human genetic disease using emerging technologies such as genome mining and novel gene therapy strategies.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the structure, organisation and functional rearrangement of eukaryotic genomes;</li>
<li>Explain the mechanism of DNA replication in eukaryotic cells;</li>
<li>Illustrate how gene expression is regulated in eukaryotes and how studies of DNA, RNA and protein levels contribute to our understanding of these processes;</li>
<li>Discuss how cell and animal models are used to build our understanding of disease processes and to develop potential therapies;</li>
<li>Describe how the application of genomic and other technologies is used to further our understanding of genomes and the treatment of disease;</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to organise, plan and successfully execute laboratory experiments relevant to advanced molecular biology, as well as analyse and report the results in a meaningful way;</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to undertake literature based research to collect and evaluate information relevant to current problems in biochemistry and molecular biology and to effectively communicate ideas in writing or orally.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 55% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Essay (2000 words): 15% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Small group/practical work: 30% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Two 1-hour lectures, one 1-hour tutorial and one 3-hour practical/ peer-group or self-directed learning exercise per week</li>
</ul><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/microbiology">Microbiology</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BFZ5959</span> - Accounting and finance for international managers<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BFZ5959">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-banking-and-finance.html">Department of Banking and Finance</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Kym Brown">Dr Kym Brown</a>
        
        (Full year)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=John Watson">Dr John Watson</a>
        
        (Second semester)
      
    <br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BFZ5959">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>Students who have completed <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BFM5959.html">BFM5959</a></span>, BFF5959, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BFS5959.html">BFS5959</a></span> or AFX9590, or enrolled in courses 0748, 0503, 0790, 0826, 3850, 4401, 4402 and 3843 are prohibited from enrolling in this unit.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides an introduction to terminology, concepts and techniques used in accounting and finance. Important areas to be discussed include understanding financial statements, basic analysis of financial statements, working capital management, the framework of capital budgeting, and time value of money. International issues in accounting will also be examined. The emphasis will be on decision making and value creation in a global environment.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>develop an understanding of the nature and roles of accounting and finance in managing in a global environment</li>
<li>explore the process of value management in a global world</li>
<li>develop competencies and computational skills required to prepare and evaluate the strategies and tactics associated with value creation</li>
<li>develop an appreciation for the relevance of theory and its linkage with practice</li>
<li>apply critical thinking, problem solving and presentation skills to individual and/or group activities dealing with principles of accounting and finance and demonstrate in an individual summative assessment task the acquisition of a comprehensive understanding of the topics covered in BFZ5959.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 40% + Examination: 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">IAR4118</span> - Interior architecture studio 8<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">18 points, SCA Band 2, 0.375 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-IAR4118">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-design.html">Department of Design</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Nicole Kalms">Associate Professor Nicole Kalms</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Charity Edwards">Ms Charity Edwards</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=IAR4118&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-IAR4118">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IAR4117.html">IAR4117</a></span> and TAD4502 or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/TAD4523.html">TAD4523</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>IAR4108</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Projects are student-generated and complex, usually addressing specialised commercial contexts. Building construction, detailing, and specifications are researched and documentation of these aspects is required as part of the project requirements. Students undertake detailed design development stemming from their earlier research studies in specific contemporary discourses and practices pertaining to their project. Students develop a fully professional resolution of all technical, philosophical and aesthetic aspects of their individual projects.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate understanding of a specialist application of interior architecture, with particular reference to relevant contemporary interior, environmental and architectural design and discourse; and the complexity of human needs that this interior architecture application addresses;</li>
<li>Competently articulate the personal aesthetic, cultural and social position represented by their design solution, in its technical resolution and detail;</li>
<li>Demonstrate application of this research-based understanding and capability in the development of a fully resolved specialist set of interior architecture designs that resolve to a high degree all project factors;</li>
<li>Be able to communicate resolution of the project with high quality presentations and professional level technical documentation;</li>
<li>Self-manage the scheduling of project work;</li>
<li>Identify, understand and be capable applying the pertinent building technologies, specifications, and documentation techniques;</li>
<li>Observe and employ occupational health and safety principles and rules appropriate to studio practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>36 hours per week including 8 contact hours plus 28 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS2992</span> - Global immersion guarantee program<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 2, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS2992">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>

<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sarah McDonald">Associate Professor Sarah McDonald</a>

<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2992&amp;tpCode=SSA-02&amp;tpYear=2019">Summer semester A</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS2992&amp;tpCode=SSB-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Summer semester B</a>
</li>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS2992">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-overseas.html">Overseas</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Summer semester A 2019 (Flexible)</li><li>Summer semester B 2019 (Flexible)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in Bachelor of Arts or Bachelor of Global Studies (including double degree students) to undertake this overseas study tour unit.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><ul>
<li>This unit is an <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad">international study program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">international study program (<a href="http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad">http://future.arts.monash.edu/learning-abroad</a>)</span> that requires an application to be enrolled and may incur additional cost.</li>
<li>The unit may be offered as part of the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html">Summer Arts Program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Summer Arts Program (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html">http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html</a>)</span>.</li>
<li>For students enrolled in the Bachelor of Global studies, this unit counts to all specialisations as an elective.This is an <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="https://www.monash.edu/pubs/2019handbooks/aos/arts-enrichment-units/index.html">Arts enrichment unit</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Arts enrichment unit (<a href="https://www.monash.edu/pubs/2019handbooks/aos/arts-enrichment-units/index.html">https://www.monash.edu/pubs/2019handbooks/aos/arts-enrichment-units/index.html</a>)</span>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit explores the impact of the global movement of people and goods on environmental sustainability. Based in different international locations, students will undertake field work with partner organisations that focus on areas such as food and water security, conservation and urbanisation, eco-tourism, the impact of key regional economic sectors on the local environment, global supply chains and environmental sustainability. The fieldwork components of this unit will allow students to apply the theoretical knowledge they gain in class to real world problems.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>recognise and explain the interplay of regional and global factors that impact environmental sustainability;</li>
<li>evaluate organisational responses to issues of environmental sustainability;</li>
<li>apply theoretical knowledge to real-world issues;</li>
<li>communicate effectively in both written and oral formats;</li>
<li>work collaboratively;</li>
<li>identify and utilise intercultural competency skills.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/arts-enrichment-units">Arts enrichment units</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">PBH2005</span> - Health program planning<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PBH2005">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-public-health-and-preventive-medicine.html">School of Public Health and Preventive Medicine</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Micaela Drieberg">Micaela Drieberg</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Micaela Drieberg">Micaela Drieberg</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PBH2005&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PBH2005">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>(<span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/HSC1200.html">HSC1200</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS1042.html">BMS1042</a></span>) AND <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/HSC2300.html">HSC2300</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>HSC2051, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH2051.html">PHH2051</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>In this unit, students will develop knowledge and skills for public health and health promotion program design and implementation.</p>
<p>These are core competencies for health promotion practice.</p>
<p>Students will develop skills in community needs assessment, determining priorities and defining target populations, and selecting an appropriate mix of strategies based on evidence and theory.</p>
<p>Strategies that take into account social and health inequalities will be examined. Students will consider key steps in implementation management and methods for building program sustainability.</p>
<p>The relationship between program planning and evaluation will be discussed, to provide students with a foundation for later studies concerning evaluation methods.</p>
<p>Case studies, group work and planning tools will be used to develop practical problem-solving skills.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the steps in planning a preventive health program;</li>
<li>Identify data sources for needs assessment and community profiles;</li>
<li>Develop a needs assessment incorporating elements of community profiling as the basis of an evidence-based program plan;</li>
<li>Identify determinants of population health needs that can be changed by health promotion action;</li>
<li>Write SMART project goals and objectives that are clearly linked to health determinants;</li>
<li>Identify administrative and management issues that need to be addressed for successful program implementation.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Health profile (1,800 words) (30%)</li>
<li>Individual oral presentation (5 minutes) (10%)</li>
<li>Intervention map (30%)</li>
<li>Project implementation plan (1,800 words) (30%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle:</p>
<p>80% attendance at seminars.</p>
<p>80% participation in weekly online tasks</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Seminar 2.5 hours, 3.5 hours of directed online student learning activities, plus 6 hours of self-directed study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/health-science">Health science</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/public-health">Public health</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3775</span> - Theatre internship unit<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3775">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-centre-for-theatre-and-performance.html">Centre for Theatre and Performance</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Felix Nobis">Dr Felix Nobis</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Felix Nobis">Dr Felix Nobis</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3775">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Two gateway units in Theatre</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>This is an <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://artsonline.monash.edu.au/internships/">internship</a><span class="hbk-print-url">internship (<a href="http://artsonline.monash.edu.au/internships/">http://artsonline.monash.edu.au/internships/</a>)</span> unit that requires an application to be enrolled.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides students with an opportunity to develop skills and knowledge by taking a responsible role within a company or organisation and observing - and reflecting upon - what happens there. The unit provides a structure by which students identify host organisations, compile appropriate applications, work an equivalence of 80-100 hrs within an organisation, and submit a set of reflections.  Students meet regularly with coordinator but are ultimately responsible for their own learning and must take a leading role in identifying, securing and participating in internships.</p>
<p>Involvement within the host institution might take the form of administrative, practical and/or creative activity.  CTP has developed working relationships with a number of potential host institutions however new proposals will be considered.  Host institutions are approved on the basis of professionalism and industry standing.</p>
<p>This unit can run at any time during the year and might fall outside semester periods.  Final submission of reflection and assessment, however, can only take place during semester.  All applications must be approved by the coordinator in advance.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>organise a professional job application, including curriculum vitae, to appropriate industry standard;</li>
<li>identify meaningful aspects of professional practice and evaluate how these dimensions exist within a theatrical organisation;</li>
<li>better understand the span and scope of professional practice and industry;</li>
<li>compile and present a comprehensive report on a theatrical institution;</li>
<li>reflect on the processes of experiential learning and articulate meaningful questions relating to the value and challenges of work-integrated learning.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/theatre-and-performance">Theatre and performance</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>First semester 2019 (Online)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (Online)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Only available to</p>
<ul>
<li>students in the Graduate Diploma of Information and Knowledge Management</li>
<li>students in the Archives and recordkeeping or the Library and information science areas of study in the MBIS or MBIS Professional.</li>
<li>students in the Library, archival and recordkeeping systems specialisation or the Corporate information and knowledge management specialisation in the MBIS or MBIS Professional.</li>
</ul>
<p>The unit is to be undertaken after 24 credit points from the GDIKM or the relevant MBIS professional tracks or areas of study have been completed.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Full-time students must enrol in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT5122.html">FIT5122</a></span> or FIT5104 in conjunction with <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT5120.html">FIT5120</a></span> in their final semester. Part-time students must complete <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT5122.html">FIT5122</a></span> or FIT5104 prior to enrolling in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT5120.html">FIT5120</a></span>, in their final semester. Only students completing the Archives and recordkeeping or Library and information science specialisations in the Master of Business Information Systems and Master of Business Information Systems (Professional) will enrol in FIT5104 in place of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT5122.html">FIT5122</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>IMS5015</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides a practical and theoretical understanding to what it means to be an information professional today. Students will encounter a range of issues relevant to professional practice in the workplace, including ethical and legal challenges caused by technology use. Through a fieldwork placement, students gain in-depth understanding of information agencies and the organisational environment in which they operate. Students will research established theories and concepts and critically evaluate their practical use (taking into account many international aspects) in organisations today, as well as reviewing and understanding the wider responsibilities that IT professionals are called upon to uphold in society. Topics addressed include - organisational and professional communication; teamwork; the nature of the information professions; the role of professional associations; problem solving and information use; cross-cultural awareness; personal and professional ethics and codes of practice. The unit addresses issues in information management and information systems currently identified by practitioners, managers, researchers, organisations, and academics as being of professional concern.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>compare and contrast IT professional roles, assessing the necessity and rationale for constant review and change;</li>
<li>identify and analyse the ethical dimensions associated with IT-related decisions, use and quality and their possible impacts on organisations and society;</li>
<li>reflect on and analyse the need for IT professional associations and the need for codes of ethics (including the ACS) in IT development and use;</li>
<li>research, select and apply strategies, protocols and innovative methods for effective and efficient communications across all stakeholders, evaluating their appropriateness for intercultural communications;</li>
<li>appraise and justify various teamwork skills for various situations, demonstrating the ability to apply them by working cooperatively and managing conflict within their team;</li>
<li>develop and apply appropriate information gathering, critical evaluation (information and its sources) and problem solving skills;</li>
<li>evaluate, assess and communicate both personal and team progress and learning, thus engaging in meaningful reflective practice.</li>
<li>apply theories and practice of selected specialisation to the workplace.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>In-semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>One 1-hour lecture</li>
<li>One 2-hour tutorial</li>
<li>One 1-hour student meeting</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Study schedule for off-campus students:

<ul>
<li>Off-campus students generally do not attend lecture and tutorial sessions, however should plan to spend equivalent time working through the relevant resources and participating in discussion groups each week.</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 8 hours independent study per week for completing lab and project work, private study and revision.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/archives-and-recordkeeping">Archives and recordkeeping</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/library-and-information-science">Library and information science</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">AZA3259</span> - Geographical information systems (GIS): Planning and decision making<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-AZA3259">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-south-africa-school-of-social-science.html">South Africa School of Social Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Agnes Babugura">Dr Agnes Babugura</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Shelter Khuzhazha">Ms Shelter Khuzhazha</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-AZA3259">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of second-year Arts units.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>AZA2259, ATS2259, ATS3259</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit introduces GIS (Geographical Information Systems) and discusses basic principles, techniques and applications of GIS in the field of geography and environmental science. It examines and reviews specific applications  where GIS is a useful tool. Subjects covered include basics of GIS, spatial data sources, spatial data quality, spatial data analysis and decision support systems. It also includes the basic principles of remote sensing and the use of satellite imagery. Cases studies and hands-on practices allow students to gain experience in the use of GIS.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the end of the unit students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate the utility of digital spatial data handling for mapping and analysis from digital data, referring to themes in environmental science;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a clear understanding of the key concepts concerning the application of GIS to environmental problems</li>
<li>Explain how value can be added to the data in any information management system with geocodes, by implementing digital spatial data analysis;</li>
<li>Be able to assess the nature of digital spatial data, offer tests for validation and descriptions of the relative value of data sets compared with (raw) data supplied by custodians;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a high level of skills in the use of GIS software (Quantum GIS, Ilwis, ArcGIS) to solve environmental problems;</li>
<li>Develop your own environmental applications of GIS ;</li>
<li>Explain how digital spatial data handling is different from other digital data handling challenges, and how the theory on which it is based is central to spatial data handling for environmental science.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 60% + Exam: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/geography-and-environmental-science---south-africa">Geography and environmental science - South Africa</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/criminology-and-criminal-justice---south-africa">Criminology and criminal justice - South Africa</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">PAR3021</span> - Paramedic emergency management<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PAR3021">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-community-emergency-health-and-paramedic-practice.html">Department of Community Emergency Health and Paramedic Practice</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Craig Taylor">Mr Craig Taylor</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Brendan Shannon">Mr Brendan Shannon</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PAR3021&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PAR3021">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-peninsula.html">Peninsula</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PAR2012.html">PAR2012</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PAR2022.html">PAR2022</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PAR2032.html">PAR2032</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PAR2020.html">PAR2020</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in course codes M20021 or M2011</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit develops the role of the paramedic as a clinical leader in the community with the focus on major incidents and disasters. The unit explores disaster planning, response and recovery, and the roles and responsibilities of the paramedic when managing multiple patients or a complex setting, during a major health emergency or during a humanitarian disaster.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the roles and responsibilities of paramedics, emergency services and other health agencies in relation to a multi-casualty or major incident.</li>
<li>Compare and contrast the management of major incident in a rural, remote or complex setting compared to the urban environment.</li>
<li>Describe the broader requirements of paramedics, emergency services and other health agencies during disaster management, in particular the management of public health issues and logistics management.</li>
<li>Analyse the contemporary structure of a major incident control system in the Australian context, and describe the role of the paramedic in major incidents and disasters, particularly compared to normal operations.</li>
<li>Outline the role of the paramedic in emergency management planning and preparedness in local and international settings.</li>
<li>Demonstrate effective logistical management, patient triage or participation in a response team during a simulated mass-casualty situation or major incident.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Mass Casualty Written Assignment (3,000 words) (40%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Mass Casualty Worksheet (1500 words) (20%)</li>
<li>Final Examination (40%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Mass Casualty Simulation (Pass/Fail) (hurdle)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>A combination of lectures, tutorials, practicals and online activities (6 hours per week), and self-directed study (6 hours per week).</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/paramedicine">Paramedicine</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">IMM2022</span> - Immunology in health and disease<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-IMM2022">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Frank Alderuccio">Associate Professor Frank Alderuccio</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Kim Murphy">Dr Kim Murphy</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=IMM2022&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-IMM2022">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM2011.html">IMM2011</a></span>* or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS2052.html">BMS2052</a></span></p>
<p class="footnote">* Note that only <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM2011.html">IMM2011</a></span> taken from 2012 onwards can be counted as a prerequisite unit - any previous versions have overlapping content and are prohibitions.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM2011.html">IMM2011</a></span> if taken prior to 2012</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The immune system has a central role in many aspects of health and disease in both humans and animals. While the immune system is critical for protecting us from pathogens, it also has an important role in cancer surveillance and is the reason why tissue transplantation is difficult to achieve. Many debilitating conditions such as allergy and autoimmune diseases including type 1 diabetes and multiple sclerosis are caused by the immune system. This unit progresses from <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/IMM2011.html">IMM2011</a></span> which focused on the development and structure of the immune system and immune response to now examine the broad role of the immune system in a range of disease and health states. By selecting a range of real life examples, we can not only examine the nature of how the immune system is active but also broaden our understanding of social and ethical implications and the role that medical research has towards improving outcomes. This unit will give students the opportunity to learn how immunology is important in many aspects of our society while developing and reinforcing a range of academic skills through defined teaching and assessment tasks.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Define the key role of the immune system in a range of human immune mediated diseases;</li>
<li>Define the mechanisms of inflammation used in a range of immune based diseases of conditions;</li>
<li>Work constructively in a group to design, research and generate a web based information site on selected areas of immunology;</li>
<li>Work within a group environment to design, research, generate and deliver oral presentations on selected aspects of immunology;</li>
<li>Apply skills developed in this unit to research, appraise and generate a written, oral or video output that focuses on a defined area of immunology.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Tutorial assessment: 25%</p>
<p>Written assessment: 15%</p>
<p>Online quizzes: 10%</p>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 50% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Two hours of lectures and three hours of tutorials/workshops per week</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/human-pathology">Human pathology</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/immunology">Immunology</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3884</span> - History of philosophy: Emotions<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3884">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-philosophy.html">Philosophy</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jacqueline Broad">Associate Professor Jacqueline Broad</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jacqueline Broad">Associate Professor Jacqueline Broad</a>
<br/>

</li>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3884">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Twelve credit points of second-year Arts units. As this is a third-year level unit, it is highly recommended that students only take this unit after they have completed two second-year level units in Philosophy.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><ul>
<li>The unit may be offered as part of the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html">Summer Arts Program</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Summer Arts Program (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html">http://www.monash.edu/students/courses/arts/summer-program.html</a>)</span>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit will examine issues to do with emotions in the history of philosophy. In the pre-modern era, the emotions or 'passions', such as love, desire, fear, and sadness, were seen as mental states that arose involuntarily in the soul as a result of its close connection with the body. They were commonly regarded as corrupting influences on an agent's moral choices and actions. To overcome their influence, philosophers recommended various techniques for either suppressing the passions or turning them into virtues or excellences of character. Following the Augustinian tradition, many regarded love as the key to transforming the passions. This unit explores the moral and metaphysical dimensions of this subject, with reference to both male and female philosophers of the past. Some of the thinkers who may be discussed include St Augustine, Rene Descartes, Elisabeth of Bohemia, Mary Astell, and David Hume. Some of the themes in the unit may be followed into contemporary philosophical discussions.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of the unit, students will have:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>gained some understanding of the history of moral philosophy, especially issues to do with the role of virtue, free will, and the emotions in the attainment of happiness;</li>
<li>reflected on some historical precedents to contemporary moral debates in virtue ethics and the emotions;</li>
<li>developed an enhanced capacity for critical and rigorous reading of a philosophical text;</li>
<li>developed skills in the evaluation of philosophical arguments in their original historical-intellectual context;</li>
<li>developed skills in writing and argument in ways that are responsive to discussion in seminars.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment:100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Off-campus attendance requirements</h2>
<div>
<p></p><p>Off-campus: no timetabled contact hours</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/philosophy">Philosophy</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BTF5910</span> - Corporate sustainability regulation<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BTF5910">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>

<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-business-law-and-taxation.html">Department of Business Law and Taxation</a></p>

<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BTF5910&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>

<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BTF5910">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (Evening)</li><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit considers legal and regulatory perspectives on global environmental challenges, and the diverse vocational skill set required to promote more sustainable business models. Topics will be drawn from current environmental controversies with particular focus upon the role of corporations and business managers.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>identify and understand the nature of global environmental challenges facing business enterprises</li>
<li>investigate and analyse a series of recent case studies exploring the effectiveness of relevant models of environmental regulation</li>
<li>investigate and analyse the legal and social obligations of corporations and business managers with respect to the environmental impacts of business activities.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 60% + Examination: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
