<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3249</span> - French individualism<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3249">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-french-studies.html">French Studies</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Natalie Doyle">Dr Natalie Doyle</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Natalie Doyle">Dr Natalie Doyle</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3249">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>At least French proficient 1</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit takes as its starting point French films of comedy and drama from the late 20th century and early 21st. These films open up a discussion of the way French culture defines individuality and its relationship to social coexistence. Written texts (literary, philosophical, critical)  are used to explore the historical roots of contemporary French culture in the court society of monarchy, notably in the 17th century as it established the cultural parameters within which French individualism developed and later shaped the creation of a Republican national culture.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon the successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>explain French individualism and its cultural specificity;</li>
<li>analyse the historical circumstances that have shaped French culture, namely the influence of monarchical absolutism and court life;</li>
<li>examine and evaluate classical texts of French literature and philosophy as well as contemporary critical texts;</li>
<li>examine and evaluate contemporary film in French from a sociological perspective;</li>
<li>apply the methodology of historical sociology to critically analyse contemporary French culture;</li>
<li>communicate in French, both orally and written, especially in the area of exposition and argumentation.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/french-studies">French studies</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">CHM2922</span> - Spectroscopy and analytical chemistry<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CHM2922">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-chemistry.html">School of Chemistry</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Alison Funston">Dr Alison Funston</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jie Zhang">Associate Professor Jie Zhang</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Lim Yau Yan">Associate Professor Lim Yau Yan</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=CHM2922&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CHM2922">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CHM1011.html">CHM1011</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CHM1051.html">CHM1051</a></span>, plus <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CHM1022.html">CHM1022</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CHM1052.html">CHM1052</a></span>. Students without these should consult the second year coordinator.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>CHM2741</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit covers the theory and instrumentation behind common physical and analytical instrumental techniques such as infrared, Raman, UV/Vis absorption and fluorescence and atomic spectroscopies, mass spectrometry, chromatography and electroanalytical chemistry. A knowledge of the physical chemistry of gases and liquids is an important precursor to the understanding of chromatographic and electroanalytical chemistry. The application of these techniques in forensic analysis is examined using examples such as the detection of accelerants at arson scenes, drug detection in sport and identification of micro samples at crime scenes. Practical exercises will provide problem solving in physical and forensic analytical chemistry. A "Moot Court" team exercise and guest lecturers are an integral part of the subject.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Comprehend concepts in instrumental analysis, including accuracy and precision, sensitivity, selectivity, detection limit and dynamic range;</li>
<li>Describe the principles and applications of spectroscopic techniques such as infra-red, Raman, UV/Visible absorption and fluorescence, and atomic mass spectrometry;</li>
<li>Demonstrate knowledge of electrochemical techniques for chemical analysis;</li>
<li>Distinguish the need for, and uses of, separation techniques such as gas and liquid chromatography;</li>
<li>Evaluate a range of instrumental methods and how different instruments operate;</li>
<li>Compare and contrast a number of case studies illustrating the many and varied uses of chemical instrumentation for solving analytical and forensic problems;</li>
<li>Use database searching and retrieval for compound identification;</li>
<li>Demonstrate expertise in the manipulation of chemicals, the use of chemical analysis techniques, risk assessment and the use of modern information technologies and data analysis;</li>
<li>Work in small groups and be competent in the written and oral presentation of scientific data, including in the context of a Moot-court scenario.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (2 hours): 40% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Mid semester test (1 hour): 20%</p>
<p>Computer test/Assignments: 10%</p>
<p>Laboratory reports: 30% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Hurdle requirement: To pass this unit a student must achieve a minimum score of 50% in the laboratory practical component and a minimum of 30% for the end-of-semester exam.</p>
<p>Supplementary assessment is not available for the lab practical component.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Two 1-hour workshops, one tutorial, one hour directed independent study and the equivalent of 3 hours of laboratory activity per week</li>
</ul><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/chemistry">Chemistry</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/medicinal-chemistry">Medicinal chemistry</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Any of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/DWG1201.html">DWG1201</a></span>, DWG1202, DWG1301, DWG1103, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/DWG1201.html">DWG1201</a></span>, or permission from Studio Coordinator</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides students the opportunity to explore the relationship between Fine Art practice and anatomy. Students will work from anatomical specimens (including prosected cadavers) at the Anatomical Museum and various forms of diagrammatic representation of the body. Through a variety of media and methodologies, the students explore how to make sense of the form and structure of the body, drawing on perceptual, observational and conceptual drawing strategies; as well as contemporary issues regarding the body found in critical theory. The unit will also address the OHS and ethical issues required for study in this area.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students should:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Have a wide graphic visual vocabulary to serve and maximise their individual expressive needs in relation to the body;</li>
<li>Have aesthetic sensibilities that enable them to critically determine imagery that bridges both historical and contemporary art;</li>
<li>Productively develop a wide variety of visual material and techniques relevant to their major discipline;</li>
<li>Have an appreciation of the structures of the body that may be of interest to the contemporary artist;</li>
<li>Have an understanding of the appropriate procedures for complying with OHS and ethical requirements in this area of study.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 4 contact hours plus 8 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is part two of the major project sequence for the honours course, and students are expected to continue with the research initiated in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS4001.html">CDS4001</a></span>, and develop a time frame which details the final visual presentation in consultation with a supervisor and the course coordinator. The project must have appropriate aspects to serve as a vehicle to demonstrate the student's professional understanding and capabilities, as well as appropriate complexity to enable the student to professionally undertake and present it within the time and resource limitations of the unit. All documentation must be completed to a professional standard.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Develop and refine their graphic design project from the conceptual stage undertaken in <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS4001.html">CDS4001</a></span> Major Project (Communication Design) Part 1 through to a visual presentation which demonstrates a very high level of capability</li>
<li>Demonstrate a comprehensive understanding of the discipline and its professional practices, with particular reference to the social, cultural and aesthetic aspects of their investigation;</li>
<li>Demonstrate a high level of knowledge of the contemporary discourse in communication design and to be able to position their work relative to it;</li>
<li>Debate and/or defend their practice in an informed critical appraisal;</li>
<li>Demonstrate they have cultivated high ambitions to perfect their research and practice in communication design.</li>
</ol>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_ada"><span class="unitcode">ADA3111</span> - Design thinking<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ADA3111">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_ada">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-ada.html">Art, Design and Architecture</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ilya Fridman">Dr Ilya Fridman</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Ilya Fridman">Dr Ilya Fridman</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ADA3111&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ADA3111&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ADA3111">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus block of classes)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ADA1111.html">ADA1111</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Design Thinking applies the skills and strategies developed by designers to a wide range of problems and situations. These skills and strategies include a range of conceptual and communication approaches, ways to explore and reconsider the context in which we work, as well as what should or could be achieved. Design thinking brings together some approaches that are known in the sciences and humanities, such as analysis and synthesis, but applies them in ways that are particular to a design approach. Design thinking can enable a more flexible approach to problem solving, and a more nuanced engagement with the complex issues of our contemporary world. This unit will introduce students to the key skills and practices associated with design thinking, and offer opportunities to explore the application of these basic creativity techniques in a range of disciplines.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Demonstrate understanding of the concepts of design thinking and their application;</li>
<li>Identify and analyse ill-defined, real-world project problems and relevant design thinking approaches;</li>
<li>Apply Design Thinking methods and approaches to a project-based problem, to develop new perspectives on key issues and to identify potential opportunties;</li>
<li>Develop, test and evaluate original proposals in response to project-based problems;</li>
<li>Develop an awareness of their preferred approaches to complex tasks, and ways these may be extended through Design Thinking.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including an average of 3 contact hours (in person or online) plus 9 hours of independent study, or equivalent.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/digital-humanities">Digital humanities</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MGF5610</span> - People management and work in a global context<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MGF5610">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-management.html">Department of Management</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sean Way">Dr Sean Way</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Sean Way">Dr Sean Way</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MGF5610&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MGF5610">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (Evening)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in course B4001, B5001, B5002, B6006, B6007, B6009 or B6012.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit analyses national differences in how people and work are managed in terms of the historical, economic, legal, political and cultural factors associated with national differences and similarities in the employment regulatory environment. Based on the premise that people are a source of competitive advantage for international organisations, employment and human resource management practices and strategies within multinational corporations are examined. Topics include; internationalisation and globalisation, divergence and convergence in national systems of employment relations in European, Anglophone and Asian countries, varieties of capitalism in these same regions, labour management practices in multinational corporations, corporate social responsibility and labour standards, regulatory and institutional differences governing the management of labour.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>critically analyse the globalisation of trade and production systems and the impact on employment relations and labour standards</li>
<li>identify the implications of globalisation for the management of labour via human resources management in different national settings</li>
<li>evaluate the work practices and labour standards in MNC's by applying ethnocentric and polycentric approaches</li>
<li>examine institutions governing trade and labour standards, including international labour standards, trade agreements, and corporate codes of conduct</li>
<li>critically assess the relationship between business, labour and government internationally.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 50% + Examination: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS3037</span> - Chinese online media: Contemporary issues and perspectives<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS3037">

         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-chinese-studies.html">Chinese Studies</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>

<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS3037&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS3037">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS2004.html">ATS2004</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS2005.html">ATS2005</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3005.html">ATS3005</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS2006.html">ATS2006</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3006.html">ATS3006</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3007.html">ATS3007</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ATS3008.html">ATS3008</a></span> or equivalent</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>ATS2037</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>This unit requires a <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/">language entry level test</a><span class="hbk-print-url">language entry level test (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/">http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/</a>)</span> or permission from the unit coordinator.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Through the study of graded Chinese news articles and audio-visual broadcasts, this unit will introduce students to the language and issues of Chinese and international contemporary affairs from a Chinese perspective. Topics covered include society, culture, politics, economics, the environment, international relations, current international events and current social issues. Students will also develop research and language skills tailored to the Chinese language Internet.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>analyse the structures of the Chinese media (written and spoken);</li>
<li>read and translate or interpret a range of Chinese news articles;</li>
<li>interpret Chinese audio-visual news broadcasts;</li>
<li>explain the political, economic, and social background to major issues in China and other Chinese speaking communities;</li>
<li>access, search, read and watch Chinese text-based and audio-visual resources on the Internet with a high degree of independence.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 55% + Exam: 45%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_arts"><span class="unitcode">ATS1208</span> - Digital Humanities: Concepts, tools and debates<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 1, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-ATS1208">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_arts">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-arts.html">Arts</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Simon Musgrave">Dr Simon Musgrave</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Simon Musgrave">Dr Simon Musgrave</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=ATS1208&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-ATS1208">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit introduces students to central concepts at the intersection of the digital world and a range of humanistic endeavours. Through case studies based in each of the themes of the major, we examine how technological possibilities have interacted with recent work in scholarship, media and heritage studies allowing exciting new techniques and methods of research and presentation of data. We consider the bases necessary for such work, the data sources and the tools, and also investigate the new communicative possibilities that result. As well as critically engaging with existing applications in the field, students in this unit will  produce digital objects presenting their own work. Through exploring the impact of technological change in this field, the unit also will foster a more general understanding of such impacts and of the inter-relation of digital technologies, society and culture.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon the successful completion of the unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>recognise and evaluate the developing role of digital technologies in society and culture;</li>
<li>analyse the impact of digital technologies on the areas of media, heritage and scholarship;</li>
<li>examine and assess examples of the application of digital technologies in the analysis and dissemination of humanities data;</li>
<li>identify complex research problems and conceptualise interdisciplinary approaches to them;</li>
<li>communicate effectively utilising both traditional and innovative means.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/digital-humanities">Digital humanities</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-AZA4778">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-south-africa.html">South Africa</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/AZA4779.html">AZA4779</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>ATS4778, AZA4311, AZA4740</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Under the guidance of an allocated supervisor, students will complete a research proposal. The research proposal will be compiled on an approved topic related to the student's chosen area of specialization. Students will meet with their supervisor on a regular basis and will be required to submit bi-monthly reports on proposal related writing assignments.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Design a research proposal under the supervision of an academic supervisor.</li>
<li>Identify a research problem, goals and questions.</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to develop and sustain an argument within the proposal.</li>
<li>Critically assess relevant primary and secondary literature in support of the dissertation topic and argument.</li>
<li>Critically assess and review relevant theories for the theoretical framework of the proposal.</li>
<li>Identify the research approaches and methodological issues relevant to the selected topic.</li>
<li>Address ethics and ethical clearance application issues.</li>
<li>Demonstrate an understanding of the methodological approaches and design and development requirements in a particular sub-discipline under investigation.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 288 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">DPSY5262</span> - Case analysis and professional practice in neuropsychology 1<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">0 points, SCA Band 1, 0.000 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-DPSY5262">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-psychological-sciences.html">School of Psychological Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Rene Stolwyk">Dr Rene Stolwyk</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Jennie Ponsford">Professor Jennie Ponsford</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=DPSY5262&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-DPSY5262">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in Doctor of Psychology in Clinical Neuropsychology</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Students will observe oral case presentations given by experienced clinicians and other students. They will be exposed to a variety of different presentation styles designed to cater for specific audiences and will learn to evaluate case material in an objective and critical manner. They will participate in discussions of clinical issues and recent developments in the field of Clinical Neuropsychology and will be challenged to remain informed about such developments and issues.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The primary aim of this unit is to provide students with an opportunity to observe and participate in oral presentations of case material and other professional issues at the same time as they commence their first clinical placement.</p>
<p>When students have completed the unit they will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>be familiar with the format of oral presentations suitable for a number of different audiences, ranging from the medico-legal forum and other colleagues to lay persons;</li>
<li>participate confidently in case discussions;</li>
<li>be informed about current issues in the field of clinical neuropsychology;</li>
<li>have developed sufficient rapport with staff members to seek assistance when it is required during later years of the course; and</li>
<li>have developed their ability to read and evaluate journal papers relevant to clinical neuropsychology.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Class Contribution 25%</p>
<p>Oral Presentation 75%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/psychology">Psychology</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">MTE2546</span> - Mechanics of materials<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MTE2546">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-materials-science-and-engineering.html">Department of Materials Science and Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Neil Cameron">Professor Neil Cameron</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Laurence Brassart">Dr Laurence Brassart</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MTE2546&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MTE2546">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit deals with the mechanical behaviour of solids subject to external loads. The basic principles of solid mechanics will be introduced, including kinematic relations, equilibrium equations and constitutive theories, in order to formulate a set of governing equations needed for solving general boundary value problems. In addition to presenting solution techniques, this unit puts emphasis on model development, since many problems in materials mechanics first require the formulation of modelling assumptions. Solid mechanics principles and modelling assumptions will be illustrated in a number of cases of practical engineering relevance, including axial and torsional loading of bars and bending of beams. Failure criteria for brittle and ductile materials (the yield criteria) will also be introduced.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the successful completion of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Describe the mechanical state of a material element using the concepts of stress and strain, starting from a physical description of the applied loads.</li>
<li>Formulate an appropriate set of governing equations and boundary conditions needed for solving solid mechanics problems, including kinematic relations and assumptions, equilibrium equations, and constitutive relations.</li>
<li>Calculate the fields of displacement, strain and stress in slender bodies subject to axial loads, torsional loads or bending.</li>
<li>Predict the onset of failure in loaded bodies using brittle fracture criteria or yield criteria.</li>
<li>Describe and compare the main features of constitutive theories for elastic, thermo-elastic and elasto-plastic behaviour of materials.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous Assessment: 50%</p>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 50%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>2 hours of lecture, 2 hours of tutorial and 8 hours of private study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p>Materials science</p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">MED3200</span> - Foundation clinical studies<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">24 points, SCA Band 3, 0.500 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MED3200">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>

<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Christopher Wright">Associate Professor Christopher Wright</a>
        
        (Clayton)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Nevein Botross">Dr Nevein Botross</a>
        
        (Malaysia)
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MED3200&amp;tpCode=FY-32&amp;tpYear=2019">Full year (extended)</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MED3200">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Full year (extended) 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul><p><a href="index-bylocation-malaysia.html">Malaysia</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Full year (extended) 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Must have completed 2 of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED2031.html">MED2031</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED2042.html">MED2042</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/GMA1010.html">GMA1010</a></span>, GMA2000.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED3100.html">MED3100</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED3062.html">MED3062</a></span>. Must be enrolled in courses M6011, M6018, 4531, 4533 or 4532.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>Students who fail to progress in MED3051 in semester 1 must discontinue from MED3200. Unit discontinuation penalites will apply.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Introductory Clinical Studies integrates the learning across <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED3100.html">MED3100</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MED3062.html">MED3062</a></span>. Learning activities specific to each specialty area will be linked to the specific clinical placement and may include lectures, tutorials, case-based learning, bed- side tutorials, practical skills sessions, and specialty teaching clinics and directed learning activities.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<p>THEME I</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Comply with the code of conduct for Monash medical students.</li>
<li>Use key ethical and legal principles to discuss and evaluate issues relevant to public health, clinical research practice, and professional standards for patient care.</li>
<li>Communicate effectively and appropriately with others in academic and clinical settings (patients, family and carers, peers, and health care professionals).</li>
<li>Interact appropriately and work collaboratively with others in clinical settings.</li>
<li>Identify, develop and use strategies to meet academic and personal challenges and needs.
THEME II</li>
<li>Explain the impact of social and environmental determinants of health on health status in marginalised groups, including the Indigenous population.</li>
<li>Evaluate available programs, interventions and community resources for prevention and health promotion to determine their suitability for a patient or community.</li>
<li>Apply key concepts in population health, epidemiology and measurement of health and disease in populations.</li>
<li>Describe how the delivery of health care services has its impact on the health of individuals at all levels of the health care system.</li>
<li>Effectively search, appraise and implement information from medical research literature, lay press and clinical practice guidelines.
THEME III</li>
<li>Explain the structure and function of the human body at cellular, organ, system and whole body levels.</li>
<li>Apply the knowledge and concepts of basic biological, psychological and social science to common and important clinical conditions.</li>
<li>Relate presenting complaints and clinical signs to common and important illnesses, conditions and disorders.</li>
<li>Explain the pathological processes and causes underlying clinical signs and symptoms for specified illnesses and conditions.</li>
<li>Discuss appropriate pharmacological approaches to the management of specified conditions and diseases.
THEME IV</li>
<li>Elicit and record an accurate clinical history appropriate for the patient and the clinical context.</li>
<li>Perform and accurately record an appropriate physical examination.</li>
<li>Synthesise symptoms and signs to determine the most likely diagnosis and relevant differentials.</li>
<li>Competently perform specified clinical procedures.</li>
<li>Explain investigations and select appropriately for the patient's presenting problems or conditions.</li>
<li>Describe management principles for specified clinical problems.</li>
<li>Effectively communicate medical information to patients.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Fieldwork</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit requires students to undertake off-campus clinical placements. In the clinical setting students will have an opportunity to apply theory to practice under supervision. Attendance is mandatory for the clinical component of each unit.Students must be aware of the faculty's Clinical Placement Guidelines.Students will not be permitted to attend any clinical placements unless they have current valid Working with Children and Police checks, and have a satisfactory immunisation status, all of which must be submitted to Faculty. </p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Objective Structured Clinical Examination (OSCE) (50%)</li>
<li>2 x Written examination - Paper 1 (3 hours) (35%) and Paper 2 (2 hours) (15%) (EMQ/EMS)</li>
<li>Attendance Hurdle: Although students are expected to have 100% attendance, the Faculty has determined 90% as a minimum attendance HURDLE requirement for specified activities. These activities are specified in the unit guide.

<p>In order to pass MED3200, students must pass the OSCE examination, pass the combined written examination and pass the attendance hurdle.</p>
<p>The Borderline Group method is used to determine the pass score and borderline range for the OSCE, and the Ebel method is used to determine the pass score and borderline range for the combined written examination.</p>
<p>The MED3200 Unit Guide contains a glossary of terms, information regarding additional assessment in this unit, and details of the specified activities for the attendance hurdle.</p></li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>2 x 18 week semesters in continuous rotations through clinical attachments.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/medicine-and-surgery">Medicine and surgery</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">NUT1102</span> - Food science<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-NUT1102">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-nutrition-dietetics-and-food.html">Department of Nutrition, Dietetics and Food</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chiara Murgia">Dr Chiara Murgia</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Elizabeth Barber">Dr Elizabeth Barber</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUT1102&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-NUT1102">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUT1010.html">NUT1010</a></span> and <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUT1101.html">NUT1101</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in course code M2001.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit will introduce food science particularly the chemistry of food components in their raw and cooked state. It will introduce food preparation and cooking skills, sensory evaluation of food, food processing, production, packaging and storage. Methods of analysing food for nutrient and non-nutrient content will be examined. Teaching will be based on interactive lectures with explicit learning objectives. These will be supplemented by tutorials to support student learning and by kitchen and laboratory practical sessions for the acquisition of basic skills in food selection, storage, preparation, cooking and food analysis.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Explain the chemistry of macronutrients, micronutrients and non-nutrients in food.</li>
<li>Describe the impact of the processing, production, packaging and storage of food on the nutrient and non-nutritive components of food and relate this chemistry to food taste, texture and palatability.</li>
<li>Describe and demonstrate the principles of safe food handling.</li>
<li>Compare and contrast Australian and International food composition data including the varying methods used to analyse nutrient content of foods and apply these data to calculate the nutrient intake of healthy individuals.</li>
<li>Demonstrate food preparation and food analysis techniques.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>6 x Laboratory &amp; kitchen practical reports (approx. 500 words each) (50%)</li>
<li>Attendance (80% of practical sessions) (Hurdle)</li>
<li>Final exam (2 hours) (50%) (Hurdle)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>6 hours contact per week plus 6 hours self directed study.</p>
<p>Weekly contact hours = 3 x 1 hours lectures, 1 x 1 hours tutorial and equivalent of 1 x 2 hours practical.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/nutrition">Nutrition</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">PBH1104</span> - Global health: Opportunities and challenges<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PBH1104">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-public-health-and-preventive-medicine.html">School of Public Health and Preventive Medicine</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Karen Richards">Dr Karen Richards</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Karen Richards">Dr Karen Richards</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PBH1104&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PBH1104">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in an Undergraduate Degree</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>HSC1112</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>In this unit, we ask you to think about the vast and growing inequities in health that exist across the world and the challenges for people living in developing countries. We explore their underlying causes including: globalisation, transnational trade, tourism, rapid development, social and political transitions, climate change, violence and insecurity. Using research reports and field experience from practical projects, we examine the wider context for working in international settings as well as the issues faced by Indigenous peoples, migrants and refugees. We explore our responsibilities as 'global citizens' and we challenge you to think about ways you could make a difference.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Identify current and future global health challenges;</li>
<li>Analyse the complex underlying causes of global health challenges;</li>
<li>Provide an explanation of why there is growing inequity in the world and reflect on the responsibility of all to address this as "global citizens";</li>
<li>Identify and critique initiatives to address global health challenges;</li>
<li>Explain and critique the Sustainable Development Goals published by UN.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Group presentation (15 minutes oral and 600 word critique) (20%)</li>
<li>Online tasks (20%)</li>
<li>Class test (1 hour) (25%)</li>
<li>Assignment (2,100words) (35%)</li>
<li>Hurdle requirement: 80% attendance at seminars</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>1 hour lecture, 2 hour tutorial,  3 hours of directed online student learning activities, plus 6 hours of self-directed study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/health-science">Health science</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/public-health">Public health</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MKF3531</span> - International marketing<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MKF3531">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-marketing.html">Department of Marketing</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Yongfu He">Dr Yongfu He</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Yongfu He">Dr Yongfu He</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MKF3531&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MKF3531">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MKF1120.html">MKF1120</a></span> or equivalent.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MKW3444.html">MKW3444</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MKB3531.html">MKB3531</a><span class="unitoffered">Not offered in 2019</span></span>.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Contemporary issues in international trade and their potential to impact on the marketing initiative of companies; the economic, political, geographic, demographic and cultural issues which influence national business environments; the conduct and outcome of market research in other countries.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>explain the issues facing the global marketplace and their influence on strategic marketing decision-making especially in the functional areas of marketing</li>
<li>critically analyse the volatile and changeable nature of international markets and be able to apply marketing theories and knowledge accordingly</li>
<li>evaluate the issues associated with market entry and the impact on long term survival in a target international market</li>
<li>critically assess alternative market entry strategies and their relative value in different markets</li>
<li>formulate marketing plans for international operations especially in the Asia-Pacific region.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 60% + Examination: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<div class="hbk-banner-box">
<h1 class="banner_sci"><span class="unitcode">PHA3042</span> - Modern drug development<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-PHA3042">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_sci">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-sci.html">Science</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Barbara Kemp-Harper">Dr Barbara Kemp-Harper</a>

<br/>
</p>

<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=PHA3042&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-PHA3042">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHA3011.html">PHA3011</a></span> and one of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHA3021.html">PHA3021</a></span>, BMS3021 or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS3031.html">BMS3031</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Modern drug development will provide the student with an appreciation of the process of discovery, testing, approval and marketing of new drugs. This will include the diseases most likely to be targeted by pharmaceutical companies for drug development; the technical issues underlying drug discovery; the role of genomics in identifying novel targets; rational drug design; the importance of screens including molecular models and high throughput screening; disease models; case studies illustrating the successful development of drugs. Career opportunities in all aspects of drug development will be highlighted.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Discuss the steps involved in the drug discovery process, including sources of drugs, how targets are identified and screening processes that can be used to test for desired activity;</li>
<li>Discuss the steps involved in developing a commercial product from a potential drug candidate, including the relevant regulatory framework and marketing considerations;</li>
<li>Critically evaluate methodologies and data from experiments in the context of the drug development process;</li>
<li>Obtain, present and interpret data from pharmacological experiments relevant to the area of drug development;</li>
<li>Source, integrate and critically evaluate the scientific literature to address an issue in the area of drug development and to communicate this orally, in written form or via a poster presentation;</li>
<li>Work both independently and as part of a team.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Examination (3 hours): 50% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Tests: 10%</p>
<p>Assignments: 15% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>Practicals and in-class exercises: 25% (Hurdle)</p>
<p>This unit is subject to the <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies</a><span class="hbk-print-url">Hurdle and Threshold Standards policies (<a href="http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html">http://www.med.monash.edu.au/policies/assessment-policy-2017.html</a>)</span> of the Faculty of Medicine, Nursing &amp; Health Sciences.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Two 1-hour lectures and three hours of laboratory or self-directed learning/ tutorial per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/pharmacology">Pharmacology</a></p>
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="notes">
<p class="hbk-heading hdg_6">Notes</p>
<p></p><p>If this is your language entry point, this unit requires a <a class="hbk-screen-url" href="http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/">language entry level test</a><span class="hbk-print-url">language entry level test (<a href="http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/">http://www.monash.edu/arts/language-entry-level/</a>)</span>.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit will introduce students to a range of texts of different genres in contemporary Chinese. Students' ability to understand contemporary China and their skills of speaking, listening and writing will be further developed through reading, translation practice, essay-writing and other activities.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The subject aims to provide students with:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>General knowledge that will enhance their understanding of contemporary Chinese culture and society.</li>
<li>The ability to comprehend and express complex ideas in both spoken and written forms, consolidating skills already acquired in Chinese proficient.</li>
<li>Strategies of cross-cultural conceptualisation, incorporating translation skills, crucial to critical thinking on a range of cultural and social topics concerning contemporary China.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 70% + Exam: 30%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/chinese-studies">Chinese studies</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">MGF5261</span> - Talent management and professions of the future<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-MGF5261">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-management.html">Department of Management</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Hannah Meacham">Dr Hannah Meacham</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>

        (Off-campus)
      
    <br/>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Brad Nash">Mr Brad Nash</a>
        
        (Evening)
      
    <br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=MGF5261&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-MGF5261">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (Evening)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Students must have passed <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/MGF5985.html">MGF5985</a></span> or equivalent, or be granted permission by the Chief Examiner to undertake this unit.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in course B4001, B5001, B5002, B6006, B6007, B6009 or B6012.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is designed to develop student understanding of how managers construct and renew a talented workforce. Content addresses building employee ability, motivation and opportunity. There is a particular focus on the management and career development of professionals. The unit addresses the theories that underpin talent management as well as talent management in practice.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>critically evaluate theoretical frameworks for talent management across global organisational settings</li>
<li>develop skills in identifying talent and evaluating the talent renewal needs of professionals</li>
<li>examine human resource management practices which influence the success or otherwise of implementing a talent management approach</li>
<li>formulate, evaluate and recommend practical solutions to talent management challenges.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 50% + Examination: 50%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_bus"><span class="unitcode">BFC5925</span> - Financial management theory<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-BFC5925">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_bus">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific

         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>

<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-bus.html">Business and Economics</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-banking-and-finance.html">Department of Banking and Finance</a></p>

<ul>

<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=BFC5925&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>

</li>

</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-BFC5925">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in course B5001, B6001, B6004, B6005 or B6015.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Topics include review of foundations of finance; financial mathematics and pricing of financial instruments; valuation and the management of long term investment and financial leverage; and theory of capital structure and dividend policy.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>understand the foundations of finance and be able to apply pricing models to the valuation of equity and debt instruments in global markets</li>
<li>evaluate investment proposals using capital budgeting techniques</li>
<li>formulate capital structure and dividend policies consistent with entities' objectives</li>
<li>develop capabilities to work effectively in a group and/or demonstrate effective individual research skills to produce professional quality business documents to solve problems related to current issues in financial management</li>
<li>demonstrate in individual summative assessment task the acquisition of a comprehensive understanding of the topics covered by this unit.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 40% + Examination: 60%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
