<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=CDS2512&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CDS2512">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-caulfield.html">Caulfield</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/COL1001.html">COL1001</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS1001.html">CDS1001</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/CDS1002.html">CDS1002</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/OHS1000.html">OHS1000</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Packaging Design is a unit specifically for those who wish to explore the application of communication design processes within the realm of 3-dimensional packaging design.</p>
<p>Packaging continues to be a prominent component of our visual landscape and this unit will require its students to critically assess its environmental impact, materiality and purpose through well-considered and appropriate design solutions. Different sector needs will be explored. For example, the specific and heavily legislated needs for medication packaging may be analysed alongside the needs of a simple grocery item.</p>
<p>Students will be required to rationalise the environmental impact of each of their project solutions, in terms of materiality, reusability and recyclability. They will also comprehend the value of packaging as both a necessity for some items (sterile medical products, for example), and a persuasive and portable brand vehicle for others (foodstuffs like tea and coffee, for example).</p>
<p>Consumer needs including usability and ergonomics will also be an important consideration for students in this unit. Both form and surface graphics will be explored in detail. In addition students will be required to comprehend and apply the legal and production requirements of their packaging design outcomes.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit students will be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Understand the place of packaging in a contemporary consumer culture;</li>
<li>Create packaging solutions for products that are responsive to environmental issues and consumer needs;</li>
<li>Create designs that reflect their understanding of packaging as a brand vehicle;</li>
<li>Create designs that merge both form and surface graphics in one successful design outcome;</li>
<li>Comprehend and apply the legal and production requirements of their packaging design solution(s);</li>
<li>Critically assess the resolution of their packaging solutions, rationalising its environmental impact, materiality and purpose;</li>
<li>Understand and apply the rules of occupational health and safety appropriate to the discipline practice.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>100% in-semester assessment</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>12 hours per week including 3 contact hours plus 9 hours of independent study.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>

<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit introduces students to the topic of globalisation and its impact on the state. Unit is divided into three parts. The first segment provides a broad conceptual introduction to globalisation. In the second, students examine the impact of globalisation on the state. In the third, students evaluate the major criticisms of globalisation.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of the unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Identify the most important debates about globalization and its likely development;</li>
<li>Explain the concept of the (nation)-state and evaluate the impact of globalization on the state;</li>
<li>Explain why globalization has produced such a diverse group of opponents;</li>
<li>Evaluate the causes and impacts of current global trends;</li>
<li>Communicate ideas and arguments in verbal form;</li>
<li>Write research reports and essays.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 60% + Exam: 40%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. A unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/global-studies">Global studies</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/global-studies-in-communication-and-media">Global studies in communication and media</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_law"><span class="unitcode">LAW4163</span> - Parents, children and the state<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 3, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-LAW4163">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_law">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-law.html">Law</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Renata Alexander">Dr Renata Alexander</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-LAW4163">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB (Hons) course in 2015 or later:</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1111.html">LAW1111</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1114.html">LAW1114</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1112.html">LAW1112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW1113.html">LAW1113</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2101.html">LAW2101</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2102.html">LAW2102</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2112.html">LAW2112</a></span>; <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW2111.html">LAW2111</a></span></p>
<p>For students who commenced their LLB course prior to 2015: LAW1100 OR LAW1101 and LAW1102 or LAW1104</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/LAW4177.html">LAW4177</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Examines legislative structures for resolving disputes between parents, children and State child welfare authorities and the difficulties which arise as the result of the divided Commonwealth/State responsibility. Examines creation of families and parent-child relationships, common law and statutory principles governing rights and responsibilities of parents, particularly the provisions of Family Law Act 1975 (Cth). Examines paramountcy of 'best interests of the child' and relevant considerations.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Students who complete this course will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>identify and evaluate a knowledge of the common law and statutory principles which govern the relations between parents and children and between children, parents and the State and develop some understanding of the way in which these laws operate in practice
b  analyse and interpret the jurisdictional issues and legal procedures relevant to the determination of such disputes

<p>c  research and evaluate theoretical and critical debates about the laws governing parents and children and the adequacy of current laws and procedures</p>
<p>d  communicate effectively and persuasively on issues relevant to family law</p></li>
<li>evaluate and reflect on some of the skills necessary for practice in this area of the law and  recognize  ethical issues they may encounter in practice.</li>
<li>learn and work autonomously and use feedback to improve their own capabilities and performance</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Final examination (3 hours writing time plus 30 minutes reading and noting time): 100% OR  final examination (2 hours writing time plus 30 minutes reading and noting time): 60% and either a research assignment (2000 words): 40% OR participation in the Family Law Assistance Program with both 2.5 days (over five x half days) practical component AND a file/court report (1500 words): 40%</p>
<p>Please note that the Family Law Assistance Program option will not be available in semester 2, 2017</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_eng"><span class="unitcode">CHE5882</span> - Biomass and biorefineries<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-CHE5882">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_eng">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-eng.html">Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-department-of-chemical-engineering.html">Department of Chemical Engineering</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Mark Banaszak Holl">Professor Mark Banaszak Holl</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Gil Garnier">Professor Gil Garnier</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=CHE5882&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-CHE5882">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (Online)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p>CHE5298</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit covers biomass reaction engineering including kinetics, reaction/mass transfer limitations, selectivity, improving reaction rates, and homogeneous and heterogeneous catalysis. The role of biotechnology including enzymatic reactions, fermentation, selectivity will also be studied together with common separation liquid and liquid-solid separation processes.</p>
<p>Global concepts relevant to biorefineries will be emphasised including the carbon cycle (micro and macro perspectives), overall sustainability of water, energy, and minimising by-products from biorefineries.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of this unit, students will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>analyse new developments in fundamental aspects of biorefineries</li>
<li>assess and critique new advances and applications for biorefineries from a technical perspective</li>
<li>evaluate and recommend an appropriate biorefining approach for various biomass feedstocks</li>
<li>review and critique recent biorefinery research literature and synthesise the findings and insights</li>
<li>create and analyse experimental data to produce an accurate and detailed report</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Continuous assessment: 60%</p>
<p>Take-home final examination (case study): 40%</p>
<p>Students are required to achieve at least 45% in the total continuous assessment component and at least 45% in the final examination component and an overall mark of 50% to achieve a pass grade in the unit. Students failing to achieve this requirement will be given a maximum of 45% in the unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>On-campus enrolments: 2 hours lectures, 3 hours tutorial and 7 hours of private study per week. 8 hours of laboratories during the semester.</p>
<p>Online enrolments: 144 hours of study</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/chemical-engineering">Chemical Engineering</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">HSC3011</span> - Contemporary health challenges<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-HSC3011">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-public-health-and-preventive-medicine.html">School of Public Health and Preventive Medicine</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>

<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Charles Livingstone">Dr Charles Livingstone</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Charles Livingstone">Dr Charles Livingstone</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-HSC3011">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of the following: HSC1081, HSC2022, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PBH2003.html">PBH2003</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/BMS1042.html">BMS1042</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH1081.html">PHH1081</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH2022.html">PHH2022</a></span></p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prohibitions</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/HSC2100.html">HSC2100</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/PHH3011.html">PHH3011</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>The unit explores global and local health challenges that are at the forefront of Australia's health sector. Students will critically examine the construction of contemporary health challenges including: the implications of global inequalities in health and health problems arising from war and terrorism and political violence such as the refugee crisis.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>On successful completion of this unit students will:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Discuss in depth some key contemporary health challenges demonstrating awareness of multiple perspectives, including the ways in which different health professions approach the issues and exploring how integrated approaches to addressing the issues may be mounted across disciplines;</li>
<li>Demonstrate understanding of key global determinants of health;</li>
<li>Consider the common and specific factors involved in the construction of various contemporary health challenges as being of 'high priority', particularly in the context of the role that evidence and other factors, including the media, play in this process;</li>
<li>Demonstrate understanding of the complex interplay of political, economic, legal and socio-cultural frameworks in shaping contemporary health challenges and how they are responded to;</li>
<li>Identify and discuss the implications of ideology, values and power bases in determining our understanding (and prioritising) of contemporary public health challenges;</li>
<li>Explore specific case studies of contemporary health challenges (global or local) and critically reflect on current strategies and approaches to responding to them.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Written outline of research topic (500 words) (15%)</li>
<li>Literature review (1,500 words) (25%)</li>
<li>Research essay (3,000 words) (50%) Hurdle</li>
<li>Class presentation (in class oral presentation) (10%)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hurdle: 80% attendance at tutorials.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>1 hour lecture, 2 hour tutorial,  3 hours of directed online student learning activities, plus 6 hours of self-directed study per week.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/health-science">Health science</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/public-health">Public health</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<h1 class="banner_it"><span class="unitcode">FIT3157</span> - Advanced web design<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">6 points, SCA Band 2, 0.125 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-FIT3157">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_it">Undergraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-it.html">Information Technology</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Thomas Chandler">Dr Thomas Chandler</a>
<br/>
</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-FIT3157">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p>Not offered in 2019</p>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>One of <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT1050.html">FIT1050</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/FIT2092.html">FIT2092</a></span> or <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/ENG1003.html">ENG1003</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>Building upon the skills learned in the Interactive media major core units (Interactive media foundations and Interactive media studios 1 &amp; 2), FIT3157 introduces students to the design and development of mobile online media using HTML5, CSS3, JavaScript and WordPress. This unit is broadly divided into three parts, with groups of four weeks comprising each part. The first and second part of the unit, students will learn the principles and practicalities of responsive web design, touch based interaction and the programming of mobile functionality and animated visual effects. The final four weeks of the unit will cover WordPress content management and theme development, the managing of custom content in WordPress and the building of dynamic WordPress sites.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>At the completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>analyse, evaluate and design responsive web layouts for touch screen and mobile devices;</li>
<li>implement mobile functionality for web applications;</li>
<li>design and develop dynamic webpages using animation and visual effects;</li>
<li>implement web sites with content management by applying an understanding of server-side concepts and client-server interactions.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>In-semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload equals 12 hours per week comprising:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="a">
<li>Contact hours for on-campus students:

<ul>
<li>One hour lecture/seminar</li>
<li>Three hours tutorial/laboratories</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Additional requirements (all students):

<ul>
<li>A minimum of 2-3 hours of personal study per one hour of lecture time in order to satisfy the reading, tute, prac and assignment expectations.</li>
</ul></li>
</ol><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/interactive-media">Interactive media</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/software-development">Software development</a></p>
<p><a href="../aos/web-development">Web development</a></p>
</div>
<!-- /.content_container--> </div>
<!-- /.content-inner__main --></div>

<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p>Students must have completed 96 credit points.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Students must be enrolled in course B2000 or associated double degree program.</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit is the capstone unit for the Bachelor of Business and as such draws together the learning and experiences gained from previous business units. The unit provides students the opportunity to demonstrate being critical and creative scholars and responsible and effective global citizens, and gain an understanding of multi-disciplinary decision-making in organisations. The opportunity is via a complex project-based programme in which cultural and ethical perspectives are also assessed. Students will develop and demonstrate their career-readiness in this unit.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>The learning goals associated with this unit are to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>demonstrate the ability to use reflective thinking with respect to the development of employment skills</li>
<li>research, synthesise, analyse, evaluate and communicate how innovative multi-disciplinary decision-making occurs in organisations.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<p>Within semester assessment: 100%</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>Minimum total expected workload to achieve the learning outcomes for this unit is 144 hours per semester typically comprising a mixture of scheduled learning activities and independent study.  Independent study may include associated readings, assessment and preparation for scheduled activities. The unit requires on average three/four hours of scheduled activities per week. Scheduled activities may include a combination of teacher directed learning, peer directed learning and online engagement.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>

<h1 class="banner_med"><span class="unitcode">NUR5004</span> - Contemporary nursing practice 4<span class="hbk-archive-only"> - 2019</span></h1>
</div>
<div id="content_container_">
<h2 class="hbk-eftsl">12 points, SCA Band 1, 0.250 EFTSL</h2>
<div class="hbk-unit-info-box" id="box-NUR5004">
<h2 class="hbk-unit-info-box__heading heading_med">Postgraduate - Unit</h2>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value">Refer to the specific
         <a href="http://monash.edu/enrolments/dates/census.html">census and withdrawal dates</a>
         for the semester(s) in which this unit is offered.</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Faculty</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byfaculty-med.html">Medicine, Nursing and Health Sciences</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Organisational Unit</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-value"><a href="index-byou-school-of-nursing-and-midwifery.html">School of Nursing and Midwifery</a></p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Chief examiner(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Scott">Mr Chris Scott</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Coordinator(s)</p>
<p>
<a href="http://staffsearch.monash.edu/?name=Chris Scott">Mr Chris Scott</a>
<br/>
</p>
<p class="hbk-highlight-heading">Unit guides</p>
<ul>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUR5004&amp;tpCode=S1-01&amp;tpYear=2019">First semester</a>
</li>
<li>
<a href="http://unitguidemanager.monash.edu/view?unitCode=NUR5004&amp;tpCode=S2-01&amp;tpYear=2019">Second semester</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble " id="preamble-NUR5004">
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<div class="hbk-preamble-icon hbk-preamble-icon_mode"></div>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Offered</p>
<p><a href="index-bylocation-clayton.html">Clayton</a></p><ul class="hbk-preamble-list__offerings"><li>First semester 2019 (On-campus)</li><li>Second semester 2019 (On-campus)</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="hbk-preamble-entry">
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Prerequisites</p>
<p><span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5002.html">NUR5002</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5003.html">NUR5003</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5011.html">NUR5011</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5022.html">NUR5022</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5033.html">NUR5033</a></span>, <span class="unitlink"><a href="/pubs/2019handbooks/units/NUR5111.html">NUR5111</a></span>.</p>
<p class="hbk-preamble-heading">Co-requisites</p>
<p>Must be enrolled in one of the following course codes: 3966, M6016</p>
</div>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Synopsis</h2>
<div>
<p>This unit provides final preparation of the student for practice as a registered nurse. Adult learning principles are applied to encourage the student to identify specific learning needs and pursue opportunities to achieve tailored educational objectives. The approach to clinical learning featured in this unit enables students to explore an area of specific interest in nursing.</p>
<p>A five week clinical consolidation placement is also included in this unit that will assist students in preparation for professional practice.</p>
<p>The increasing importance of professional portfolios for the purpose of maintaining and demonstrating competency will be emphasized in this unit.</p>
<p>A focus on principles of clinical leadership, therapeutic and professional communication, multidisciplinary team work, and clinical decision making will enable consolidation and application of prior learning in this course facilitating the transition from student to professional nurse.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Outcomes</h2>
<div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this unit, students should be able to:</p>
<ol princestart="0" start="1" type="1">
<li>Explain the principles of clinical management for patients with advanced cardiac and respiratory illness.</li>
<li>Reflect on and identify specific learning needs in preparation for registration as a professional nurse;</li>
<li>Utilise adult learning theories, concepts and principles to identify specific learning needs and strategies by which these can be met;</li>
<li>Apply effective decision making frameworks to the identification and management of practice based problems and issues;</li>
<li>Develop and implement patient centred care interventions that encompass patients' cultural, ethical and developmental needs;</li>
<li>Reflect critically on personal and professional development in preparation for practice as a registered nurse;</li>
<li>Demonstrate readiness for beginning practice in accordance with, Nursing &amp; Midwifery Board of Australia Registered Nurse Standards for Practice, Code of Ethics and Code of Professional Conduct for Nurses, and;</li>
<li>Develop evidence of competency through the development of a professional portfolio.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Fieldwork</h2>
<div>
<p>Clinical placement: 200 hours.</p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Assessment</h2>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Learning contract (2000 words) (20%)</li>
<li>Clinical performance (200 hours) (40%) (hurdle)</li>
<li>Pre-clinical laboratory sessions - compulsory 100% attendance</li>
<li>Must complete clinical placement (240 hours)</li>
<li>Conference presentation (15%)</li>
<li>Professional portfolio (3500 words) (25%)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">Workload requirements</h2>
<div>
<p>8 hours a week: 4 hours lectures, 4 hours tutorials over 8 weeks. In addition, students will be required to undertake 200 hours of clinical placement.</p>
<p>Please note: Students who undertake this unit in the summer semester will be on campus for 5.5 weeks intensive mode.</p><p>See also <a href="http://www.monash.edu.au/timetables/">Unit timetable information</a></p>
</div>
<h2 class="hbk-heading">This unit applies to the following area(s) of study</h2>
<div>
<p><a href="../aos/nursing">Nursing</a></p>
<p>Nursing and midwifery</p>
</div>
